A Look at Shandong Province's Revenue, Past and Present 79

▲ The Salt Industry: Past and Present

▲ Sharp Decline in National Tax Revenue

Jinan Correspondence: Shandong Province has been known for its fish and salt resources since ancient times. Guan Zhong used this to dominate the state of Qi. Salt tax alone reached a staggering seven million yuan in the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, greatly benefiting national revenue. At that time, the salt tax was only two yuan and five jiao per dan (100 jin). In recent years, frequent wars have disrupted transportation. In salt-producing areas, salt merchants cannot transport salt out, and in salt-consuming areas, people are even at risk of lacking salt. As a result, salt tax revenue has plummeted. The current Salt Transport Commissioner, Wang Zhanghu, has been actively seeking to rectify the situation since taking office. According to Wang, the current salt tax is four yuan per dan, but due to the impact of the war, only 250,000 yuan was collected in September (excluding the fine salt from Qingdao and Yantai, which is directly taxed by the Ministry), which is more than half of what it used to be. The biggest reasons are the lack of vehicles to transport salt and the prevalence of smuggled salt. After deducting the monthly expenses of 40,000 yuan for the Audit Office, the Salt Transport Commissioner's Office, and various salt fields, as well as the 40,000 yuan for foreign debt payments, only about 150,000 to 160,000 yuan is remitted to the central government each month. Now that the war has ended and the province is unified, revenue should improve significantly this month. The rectification measures include eliminating loopholes internally and cracking down on illegal salt production externally. The province's salt industry is divided into Lu coast, Yu coast, Wan coast, Su coast, and Qing salt. The Lu coast includes twenty counties along the coast from Ju County and Rizhao to Dengzhou and Laizhou, as well as Anqiu and Zhucheng, which are the East Coast and operate on a private transport and sale basis. Qing salt is produced in Qingdao and sold exclusively to foreign markets. Both have not been affected by the war. The network merchants belong to the East Outline Public Office: (1) Dingli Company, whose outline stretches to five counties including Mengyin, Linqu, Boxing, Changle, and Xintai, has been suspended for a long time due to the impact of the war. (2) Dingxin Company, whose outline stretches to eleven counties including Guancheng, Fan County, Chaocheng, Shouzhang, Yuncheng, Heze, Dingtao, Chengwu, Jinxiang, Teng County, and Yi County, has had little business due to being in the war zone. (3) Dingyu Company, whose outline stretches to eight counties including De County, Yucheng, En County, Wucheng, Linqing, Qiu County, Tangyi, and Xin County, has also experienced poor business due to the same reasons. In addition, the seven counties of Shouguang, Linqu, Bin County, Putai, Lijin, Guangrao, and Yidu operate on an official-supervised and merchant-sale basis. Wudi, Yangxin, and Zhanhua have always been contracted by Yifeng Company, and Linyi, Tancheng, Fei County, and Yishui have always been contracted by Xiehe Company. The remaining forty-seven counties, including Licheng, also operate on a merchant-sale basis. The nine counties under the jurisdiction of Guide Prefecture on the Yu coast, including Shangqiu, Ningling, Sui County, Yongcheng, Yucheng, Xiayi, Zhecheng, Luyi, and Kaocheng, as well as the two counties of Su County and Guoyang on the Wan coast, and Tongshan County on the Su coast, have always been contracted by Gongli Transportation Company, which is known as South Transport. Due to the impact of the war in recent years, it has been suspended for a long time, and the people in various counties often suffer from a lack of salt. Recently, General Commander Chiang ordered the Jinpu Railway to allocate two trains to transport salt from Haizhou to provide relief. Shandong's salt tax has naturally suffered a great loss. However, the four counties of Feng County, Pei County, Xiao County, and Dangshan on the Su coast are contracted by Luchang Company and are still struggling to maintain operations. Such is the general situation of Shandong's salt affairs. The method of rectifying the wasteland counties is to re-invite merchants to contract with the various companies that have been suspended, and to find ways to reorganize those with poor business. As long as the war stops, military and private transportation is cut off, transportation is restored, and banditry is eliminated, Shandong's salt affairs are not without solutions. It is expected that the salt tax revenue for this month can reach about 300,000 yuan.

Furthermore, since the great war in Shandong, the province has not recovered its vitality, and various industries have declined. The impact on various tax revenues, especially national tax revenues, has been the greatest. On the 15th, the reporter visited Chen Jiadong, the financial commissioner and director of the tobacco and alcohol affairs bureau, at the financial commissioner's office to inquire about the national tax revenue and rectification plans. According to Chen, he was ordered to come to Shandong to serve as the financial commissioner and director of the tobacco and alcohol affairs bureau. After taking over in Jinan, it has only been a week, and all affairs have not yet been fully arranged. He is currently reviewing the situation of the previous tax bureaus to prepare for rectification. The original expenses of the Shandong Financial Commissioner's Office were more than 10,000 yuan. Currently, the Ministry of Finance has cut the expenses of the Financial Commissioner's Office in order to save expenses, and the expenses of the Shandong Tobacco and Alcohol Affairs Bureau are used as the expenses of both the Commissioner's Office and the Affairs Bureau, with only more than 6,000 yuan per month. Because expenses are so difficult, the Tobacco and Alcohol Affairs Bureau has moved to the Commissioner's Office. All the staff of the Commissioner's Office are also staff of the Tobacco and Alcohol Affairs Bureau. The former section chiefs are also section chiefs, and the former staff members are also staff members, in order to save expenses. At present, after the military affairs in Shandong, the income of each bureau has been greatly reduced. Those who used to earn 100,000 yuan now only earn 10,000 or 20,000 yuan. Compared before and after, the ratio is ten to one, so that the income is not enough to cover the local expenses. It may be possible to increase it slightly in about one or two months. Many of the staff of the tax bureaus in various counties are currently temporarily appointed by the military, and it is inevitable that there will be inconsistencies in the procedures. They are currently contacting everything separately. Chen plans to visit the bureaus in various places after the Jinan affairs are arranged, in order to find ways to rectify them. Regarding the employment of personnel, he plans to adopt an examination system. The Financial Commissioner's Office originally had more than 50 staff members, the Tobacco and Alcohol Affairs Bureau originally had more than 30 staff members, and about 100 people came from Jiangxi with Chen Jiadong. Currently, in order to meet the budget, only more than 30 people have been selected and the rest have been laid off in order to save expenses. He also plans to recruit some graduates from Shandong Commercial School, provide them with subsidies, and come to the office to practice. After gaining some experience, they will be appointed to positions. Extra attention should be paid to the division of national and local taxes to clarify the boundaries. (October 15)

Post-War Inspection Report of the Longhai Railway 80

▲ As Described by the Xuzhou Press Inspection Group

Xuzhou Correspondence: The Central Army fought for the longest time and most fiercely on the Longhai Railway. Now that the war has ended, the Xuzhou press organized a post-war inspection group, which departed westward on the day after the Double Tenth Festival to inspect the war remains. The details of the journey are recorded as follows:

▲ Battle Trenches Along the Way: The reporter group departed westward from Xuzhou at 1 PM on the 11th, attaching themselves to a Xu-Zheng passenger train. The passenger cars were extremely crowded, and the train moved slowly. By the time they reached Dangshan, night had already fallen. Upon reaching Dangxi, they found a prepared battle trench of the Central Army. At 10 PM, the train passed Guide, which was the site of the initial fierce battle during the military campaign. West of the station, there were one or two small battle trenches along the way across Xiaoba to Liuhe, but it was impossible to distinguish whether they belonged to our side or the enemy. Liuhe was where Commander-in-Chief Chiang supervised the battle. Near the station, there were one or two small forests. People at the station said that the Commander-in-Chief often stayed in the forest during the hot summer. The train stopped on three tracks. This place had a lot of sand and water was not readily available, so the hardship was indescribable. Continuing west, the train passed Libaji and Yejiagang, and there were more and more trenches along the way. From here, past Neihuang to Lanfeng, was where the Yan-Feng army's defenses were the most solid and where the Central Army's final fierce battle took place, so they paid close attention to observation. At this time, the moon was just waning and hanging high in the sky. Because this place had a lot of wind and sand, the light was faint, but when it shone on the ground, it could be seen very clearly. The ditches and slopes nearby could be clearly distinguished. About fifteen li east of Neihuang, there was a large battle trench of the Yan-Feng army, about one zhang deep and wide, spanning both sides of the railway. Behind the trench were machine gun positions, soldier positions, and communication trenches. About six or seven li east of Neihuang, there was also a large battle trench, whose construction was roughly the same as the previous trench. It was said that these two trenches were mostly for infantry to ambush. A particularly large battle trench was outside the Neihuang station, about one zhang seven or eight chi deep and wide. The earth fort behind the trench also seemed higher. The artillery positions, gun positions, infantry positions, communication trenches, and rest covers behind the fort were intertwined and indistinguishable. The fiercest battle between the two armies took place here, and the final outcome also depended on this trench. Unfortunately, the passenger train continued to move forward, and the Neihuang station was desolate, so it was inconvenient to get off and stay overnight. They continued to follow the train. East of Lanfeng, they found two more large battle trenches of the Yan-Feng army. Viewed from the train, the communication trenches behind the fortresses behind the trenches curved and slanted out, like plum blossom petals. Therefore, scholars called it the plum blossom trench. In total, these five large battle trenches all spanned the railway line, which was endless. It was said that it extended north to the Yellow River and south beyond Qizhou to approach the Pinghan Railway. There were also several small battle trenches distributed in the area of Libaji and Yejiagang and between the five major battle trenches. One can imagine how much labor the Yan-Feng army spent building this. The area along the way was mostly sandy, and the villages were very sparse. In the Neihuang area, even when straining their eyes to look far into the moonlight, they could not see forests or villages. The desolate scene was indescribable. At 4 AM on the morning of the 12th, they arrived at Lanfeng Station. Apart from the ticket office on the platform, there were no inns. The reporter group went to the Xushang United Relief Team office of the Gospel Church behind the station for temporary accommodation.

▲ Visiting Lanfeng: At 8 AM on the morning of the 12th, the reporter group went to inspect Lanfeng City, which was north of the station, less than a li away. It was built of brick, and the battlements were very incomplete, but it was due to years of disrepair and not due to shelling. The city was extremely desolate. There was only one cross street, which reached the four gates. Along the street, there were many dilapidated and deserted empty rooms with no occupants. Inside the South Gate was the Zhongshan Bridge, and the water flow was quite wide and deep. Occasionally, three or five small boats could be seen paddling in it. Standing on the bridge, one could see the east and west cities, and the vastness of the land could be known. The county government was dozens of steps inside the South Gate, and the scale was extremely simple. The reporters sent in their name cards to visit, and County Magistrate Fang Tinghan had just returned from Bian. According to him, he was appointed by Zhang Fang, the acting chairman of the temporary provincial government, and took office on the 27th in Qinzhai, the fifth district of southern Lanfeng. The Central Army captured Lanfeng on the morning of the 30th, and he entered the city to take office on October 1st. After the Feng army retreated from Neihuang, they only resisted once in the east and west Gangtou Villages of the city on the 29th before collapsing westward. The Central Army's Fan Xiji's troops were the first to enter Lan City on the morning of the 30th. The Feng army left a covering force in Sanyizhai, 25 li west of the city, and were defeated by the Central Army's pursuit troops on the night of the 1st. On the 2nd, the Feng army completely left Lan territory. When the war first started, Lanfeng was the defense zone of the Jin army, and Xu Yongchang was stationed here. After two fierce battles, it was replaced by the Feng army, which was garrisoned by Sun Liangcheng. When the Feng army finally retreated, Sun commanded the retreat. The disaster situation after the war was extremely serious. The Provincial Relief Association has sent personnel to investigate. The total length of battle trenches dug in the territory reached more than 720,000 chi. The plan is to use labor as a substitute for relief and employ civilians to fill them in, requiring more than 22,000 taels of silver. Because the Jin army had forced the digging of battle trenches and demanded livestock when they first arrived, many people fled. Most of the farmers who remained had no livestock to cultivate. Currently, only five out of ten people have returned to their villages after the war. The Feng army demanded 200,000 dan of wheat before retreating and now demands 20,000 yuan, ordering the district chiefs to do so, otherwise they will be put in shackles and imprisoned. The people's strength has been exhausted, and about half has been supplied. Sixty prisoners have been released. Local seasonal diseases are prevalent. The bodies on the battlefield have been treated and buried by the Xushang Mulian Association Relief Team. The police team's guns were confiscated by the Feng army, and only the standing militia is maintaining law and order. Bandits are rising up in the four villages, and the county government is unable to send teams to suppress them, which is extremely worrying. Commander-in-Chief Chiang visited Lan City on the 2nd, accompanied by Ma Fuxiang, Zhang Zhijiang, Chen Tiaoyuan, and Shao Lizi. At that time, Fan Xiji was stationed at the county government. Chiang and others stayed at the county government for two hours and then returned to the train. Afterwards, Fan's troops and Ruan Zhaochang's and Jin Handing's troops all advanced westward over the city. The supplementary troops of Chen Tiaoyuan's troops are currently stationed there. According to statistics, there are less than 2,000 households in Lancheng, which is a third-class county in Henan Province. The local products are only peanuts and small amounts of salt. The land is barren, and the war has made it even more difficult. It will take time to recover.

▲ Inspection of Gangtou: At 1 PM, guided by officials from the county government, we went to West Gangtou to inspect the battle trenches. The Red Swastika Society Relief Team also went to investigate. This place is eight li east of the city and is the last defensive fortification of the Feng army to protect the city and station. The ground is sandy and mixed with alkali flats, but the fortifications are extremely solid. The outer moat is about one zhang deep and about eight chi wide. Behind the moat is an earthen barrier, connected to the back wall of the outer moat, with an extremely steep slope. Machine gun positions are arranged on the barrier, followed by soldier positions, followed by communication trenches, followed by rest cover trenches. In addition to the outer moat, deer sheds and electric nets were temporarily set up, totaling seven layers. The solidity of the fortifications is truly rare. This moat runs south across the railway line and north to the Yellow River dike. Battle trenches and communication trenches are intertwined on the dike. According to the villagers, this moat was built by civilian labor. The Feng army captured laborers and forced them to dig, giving them two meals a day. Each meal consisted of two wheat cakes, which were not enough to eat, let alone wages, so many people fled. When the war first started, the Central Army had attacked as far as the east of this moat, but were repelled by the Feng army's counterattack. This time, they broke through this moat and captured Lancheng. Dozens of steps west of the battle trench is a small village. The Jin army generals lived in the villagers' houses, piling thick earth outside the houses to avoid shooting. The back of the house also served as a cellar, covered with thick earth to avoid the bombing of aircraft. There are only three or five houses in the whole village. The reporter personally saw that the villagers ate sorghum cornbread. The outer skin was purple-black due to excessive dryness and hardness, and it was rough and unpalatable. They drank thin sorghum porridge, which was also not like human food. Upon inquiry, it was learned that there was no wheat production in this area, and it was impossible to find anyone selling wheat flour. Just getting enough to eat was enough to make them feel safe. The observations here are enough to show the suffering of the people in the war zone. Behind the battle trench, close to the east of the city, there are many graves of the Feng army, about a thousand in total. They all have wooden markers indicating the soldiers of the Sixth Army of the Third Route Army, which is shocking. The ground along the way is mostly alkaline, and the villagers have dug salt ponds to dry and sell small amounts of salt. Upon inquiry, it was learned that the soil here is absolutely unsuitable for farming. In addition to sweeping salt earth and drying salt, they plant fragrant willow to provide fuel. The barrenness of the land is evident. According to the guides from the county government, Lanfeng and Yifeng were originally two counties. The breach of the river at Yifeng led to the merger into one county. The county's administrative expenses are only 702 yuan per month. Most of the county has this type of soil. Only a small part of the southern territory, in the fifth and seventh districts, can grow wheat, but the amount is also extremely small. After the inspection, we returned to our residence and went to Lanfeng Station, where we saw two cellars of the Yan army generals, one west of the platform and one east of the platform. The one west of the station was extremely solidly built, with wooden beams running across and covered with a large number of earthen bags. It was the residence of Xu Yongchang. The one east of the station was smaller in scale and was the residence of a middle-ranking general. It was said that the cost of Xu's cellar was 500 yuan. The intensity of the Central Army's aircraft activity can be seen from this. According to Chen Zhaoran, the head of the Xuwanzihui Rescue Team, the work of burying corpses between Lanfeng and Neihuang has not yet been completed. According to the investigation, the Feng and Jin armies relied on these solid fortifications to defend as hard as they could, while the Central Army often charged towards the battle trenches with bayonets, breaking through their electric nets and deer sheds, and rushing to the battle trenches. When the Feng army's machine guns opened fire, the Central Army jumped into the battle trenches and climbed up the fortresses. The Feng army threw grenades down with their hands. Because of this, there were many sacrifices, but the morale of the Central Army was not diminished at all, and they finally won. At present, malaria is prevalent in the countryside. Each village needs 170-80 bags of rescue medicine, which is almost the case for every village. It is truly a great calamity.

Wuhu Quick News 81

▲ The defense of Wuhu has been taken over by the 341st Regiment of the 57th Division. Xu Guoting, the regimental commander of the regiment, convened a public security meeting at the regimental headquarters today. Attendees included the chief of the public security bureau, the head of the chamber of commerce, the head of the detective team, and the presidents of various hospitals. It was agreed that the existing No. 5 and No. 26 military hospitals in Wuhu have no less than one or two thousand wounded soldiers, and restraint is extremely important. The number of soldiers going out each day is limited to one hundred, and those without permits will be arrested. In addition to implementing inspections of passengers and hotels on the upper and lower Yangtze River steamers, the regiment will send troops to guard the Yuemen Alley, Dahua Garden, and Dama Road every night for prevention.

▲ Large groups of bandits have been discovered in Xuancheng, Langxi, and Guangde in southern Anhui. The Xuancheng Bijiaqiao Public Security Bureau had guns and equipment looted by bandits.

Page 10

Upon the request of the representatives of Langxi and other counties, the 341st Regiment of the 57th Division stationed in Wuhu, under the telegram order of Division Commander Yue Shengxuan, decided to send a battalion of troops to Xuancheng tomorrow. Three small steamers, including the Taihe, have been chartered to transport them for suppression.

▲ Tang Shaogao, the chief of the Wuhu Municipal Public Security Bureau, has been transferred to the province and replaced by Zhao Jingshi. Zhao arrived in Wuhu earlier and was about to take office, but Chen Tiaoyuan went to Nanjing and summoned him to go there. He returned to Wuhu yesterday and took office at 10 AM this morning. In addition, Sun Gongming, the county magistrate of Wuhu County, has resigned due to illness. He received a telegram from the province last night to be transferred to Langxi, and Yu Yuying has been appointed as the successor in Wuhu.

▲ In order to understand the province's self-defense capabilities, Zhu Xi, the director of the Civil Affairs Department of the Provincial Government, telegraphed all counties to investigate and report the number of soldiers, firearms, and horses of the Security Corps and the self-defense groups that have not been reorganized, as well as the establishment expenses, within five days for verification.

▲ The Provincial Education Department has appointed district commissioners to conduct on-site clearing of education funds in Anhui Province. Xie Zhen has been appointed to Wuhu, Xuancheng, and Dangtu counties. Xie has arrived in Wuhu and will go to Xuan Dang after the matter is completed. (October 16)

▲ Li Mingyang wired the Provincial Security Department yesterday, stating that he had been conducting operations against the sea bandits in Xinyang Port for several days, killing nearly a hundred people and seizing many ships and goods. He is currently registering them for claims.

Reports indicate that tobacco seedlings have been found in the Hai Fu Town of Haimen County, the Third District of Lianshui County, the Zhao Zhuangji of Feng County, the Third and Eighth Districts of Pi County, the Zhoujiagou of Guanyun County, the Third, Sixth, and Eighth Districts of Shuyang County, and the Chenghou, Dongying, and Xiying villages of Donghai County. Orders have been issued to eradicate them.

▲ The Zhenjiang Land Reclamation and Mulberry Planting Committee held a meeting at the county government yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM and resolved: (1) The Sibaidu Land Reclamation and Mulberry Planting Experimental Zone must completely dig ditches and plant mulberry trees before December of this year; (2) If unable to cultivate, it can be leased to others for cultivation; (3) If willing to cultivate themselves, the mulberry seeds will be provided by the committee, and personnel will be dispatched for guidance; (4) If they neither cultivate themselves nor lease to others, the land will be surveyed and confiscated after the deadline. The above cases will be announced immediately, and strict enforcement within the time limit will be carried out. (18th)

Local Correspondence

Fengxian 83

A False Alarm in Ruanxiang Town Yesterday: Ruanxiang Town, under the jurisdiction of this county, has been like a startled bird since being subjected to two robberies. Yesterday morning, a rumor suddenly arose in the town, claiming that Taibao Ashu would lead a team to rob the town soon. As a result, merchants and residents were greatly alarmed and immediately requested the police detachment stationed in Zhuangxing to go to protect the town. The rumor also caused much anxiety in Zhuangxing. After a thorough investigation and confirmation by the police team that there was no such thing, people were relieved. However, people in both towns were quite frightened.

Suzhou 84

The Opening of the Appeal in the Sino-Foreign Lawsuit: In 1927, the British firm Xiangmao Foreign Firm, located at No. 2 Guangdong Road, Shanghai, had Bian Xiaoqing, the vice president of the Nanjing Xiaguan Chamber of Commerce, who, entrusted by the Zhili-Shandong army, ordered 30,000 bags of Saigon rice from Yang Huanqing, the firm's resident manager in Nanjing, to be used as military rations. He immediately remitted the money through the Nanjing Zhongjiao Banks. However, as the revolutionary army approached Nanjing, Bian went to the Zhongjiao Banks to stop the remittance. He explained to the bank manager that the revolutionary army had arrived in Nanjing, and the Zhili-Shandong army had retreated. He requested the head office be telegraphed to sell the Saigon rice in Shanghai, and he, the customer, would bear all losses. After the bank sold off half of the rice, the total loss amounted to over 110,000 yuan. The firm then sought Bian for compensation, but Bian avoided meeting them. Last year, Xiangmao Foreign Firm filed a lawsuit against Bian with the Jiangning County Government to recover the money. On November 23rd of that year, a judgment was issued, ordering Bian Xiaoqing to return the lost funds to Xiangmao Foreign Firm. After the judgment, Bian, arguing that Sino-foreign lawsuits should be under the jurisdiction of either the Ministry of Foreign Affairs or the judicial organs, hired Zheng Yuxiu, Li Xinyang, and Guo Dingsen as lawyers and filed an appeal with the High Court. They argued that the case should not have been judged arbitrarily by the Jiangning County Government and that the matter was under the jurisdiction of the special municipality. They requested a preliminary judgment on the jurisdictional issue. The appellee, Xiangmao Foreign Firm, also hired Wang Fuchang as a lawyer to prepare a defense. After accepting the case, the High Court, under the jurisdiction of Li Mian, the presiding judge of the Second Civil Division, repeatedly summoned both parties to court for investigation. Yesterday (the 18th), the court summoned An Fo Lai, the head of the import department of Xiangmao Foreign Firm, and Bian Xiaoqing, the appellant, as well as the agents, Zheng Yuxiu, Li Xinyang, and Guo Dingsen, as lawyers, and Baker (a foreigner), the manager of the appellee, Xiangmao Foreign Firm, and Wang Fuchang, as lawyers, to court. Bian Xiaoqing and the two lawyers, Baker, Zheng and Li, did not report. At 2:00 PM, Judge Li presided over the hearing and declared the debate on the jurisdictional issue closed, setting the verdict for the 22nd of this month.

The Dispute Over the Public Property of the Chen Hengfeng Store: The Chen Hengfeng Store, located in the Xibaihua Lane inside the gate, is the estate of a prominent Suzhou gentleman, with 2,000 mu of family-supporting farmland. The store manager of the second west branch has been collecting rent to support the poor members of the clan. Cheng Fujin, a member of the clan, recently sought to request the store to make public the accounts of the family-supporting farmland due to financial difficulties. The store's accounting house refused. The First Sub-bureau was informed on the 17th and summoned Cheng Jinpu to the First Sub-bureau and transferred him to the District Court. The prosecutor's office investigated the matter that evening and summoned Xu Xingzuo, the store's accountant, for questioning. Considering the matter a family dispute, they advised Xu Xingzuo to take Cheng Jinpu back and be responsible for making the accounts public in order to be credible.

Wujiang 85

The Resolution of the Shengze Silk Tax Collection Problem: The Shengze Town Silk Tax Office in this county previously promoted the sale of customs treasury bonds by levying an additional 20% on silk donations. The silk merchants opposed this, and the tax office responded by detaining goods to force donations, which led to a five-day market shutdown. Now, Director-General Hu Songshan has gone to Shengze to negotiate and has reached an agreement. Starting from the date of the resolution, the silk industry association will collect 20% monthly based on the total production and sales volume of each firm until the end of November. No more collections will be made after that.

The Dismissal of the Tongli Public Security Sub-bureau Chief: Dai Yingzhen, the chief of the Second Public Security Sub-bureau in Tongli Town, this county, was reported by the First District Party Department. After investigation by Director Zhou, the report was found to be true, and Dai was ordered to be dismissed. Zhang Xin, the chief of the Judicial Section of this bureau, has been appointed to act as his replacement.

Wuxi 86

A Japanese Buddhist Pilgrimage Group Visits Wuxi: A Japanese Buddhist Youth Association pilgrimage group, consisting of about fifty men, women, and children, arrived in Wuxi from Shanghai yesterday morning. They visited scenic spots such as Meiyuan, Taihu Lake, and Yuantouzhu, and surveyed and mapped the area. They returned to Shanghai by car at 6:00 PM in the evening.

A Double-Crosser Cannot Escape the Law: A guest merchant, Mei Fengjin, has been trafficking red pills for a living. Recently, he entrusted Fu Arong (also known as Crippled Arong), who lives at No. 61 Zhongzheng Road, to go to Shanghai and bring back a large batch of 88,000 red pills, worth five or six hundred yuan. However, Arong swallowed all the pills. When Fengjin found out, he negotiated with Arong. Arong, feeling guilty, fled to Shanghai. Around midnight the night before, Arong returned to Wuxi from Shanghai and stayed with his wife, Gu, at the Su-Xi Hotel on the road. Coincidentally, Inspector Wang Xiezong of the Public Security Bureau was inspecting rooms there and caught sight of Arong. He immediately reported to Inspector Hu, who reported to Director Xu of the Public Security Bureau. Director Xu immediately dispatched detectives Shen Minhua and Tang Yaoting to assist in the arrest. Arong and his wife, Gu, were both arrested and taken to the bureau for interrogation. Unexpectedly, when they were being escorted to the intersection of Zhongzheng Road, Gu, Arong's wife, injured Detective Tang Yaoting's head and wrists and lost a flashlight. Fortunately, the police officers at the post assisted in sending the Arong couple to the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, Director Xu transferred them to the county government for legal action.

The Water Police District Dispatches Warships to Strictly Guard Against Lake Bandits: Mao Mujun, the chief of the Second District of the Waterborne Provincial Public Security Team stationed in Wuxi, because Taihu Lake has always been a den of bandits, and the East and West Mountains and the Three Mountains are the easiest places for bandits to gather. Now that it is winter defense season and public safety is important, yesterday he instructed Tang Peng, the captain of the Zhaowu warship, to set sail for the area to patrol.

Four People Released in a Kidnapping Case in Two Townships: On the 6th of this month, Dengjiawan and Xiaoqiaotou, two towns bordering the Second District (Jingyun City) and the Twelfth District (Taibo City) in this county, were searched and robbed by bandits, who kidnapped seven men and women. Except for Ling Renda and Ling Baoxian, who were released earlier, the others have not yet been released. The victims' families received letters from the bandits demanding a ransom of 250,000 yuan. After repeated negotiations, the price was reduced to 110,000 yuan, but no results have been achieved. It is now learned that four of the five hostages were released yesterday. The remaining one will be released after the conditions are agreed upon. In addition, Feng Yuequan, the fifteen-year-old son of Feng Yunsheng, the deputy head of Shuiqu Township in the Fourth District (Kaiyuan Township), was kidnapped by bandits at midnight on the 24th of last month. More than two weeks have passed since then. A letter was received from the bandits the other day, stating that the hostage is now in a certain place in Jiangyin. They demanded that he be taken for negotiation immediately and demanded a ransom of 10,000 yuan. After receiving the letter, Feng Yunsheng immediately sent someone to negotiate with the bandits to negotiate the price for the ransom.

The Urgent Need to Install Telephones in the Four Townships: Yao Dixing, the director of the Wuxi County Construction Bureau, previously initiated the installation of telephones connecting the four townships to the city to facilitate communication between the city and the countryside. He prepared a plan and budget and submitted it to the county government for forwarding to the Department of Construction for approval. However, due to the lack of approval, it was not implemented. Recently, Director Yao has repeatedly received letters from various district offices, requesting that the township telephone system be installed according to the original plan in order to facilitate communication. After receiving the letters, Director Yao believes that it is indeed necessary to install telephones in the four townships. Therefore, he is proceeding with the original plan. The expenses required are to be borne half by the installing townships and districts, and the other half is to be subsidized from the construction special donation fund, following the precedent of subsidizing the long-distance telephone expenses connecting Wu County. Yesterday, Director Yao submitted the plan to County Magistrate Pan for review and forwarding to the Department of Construction for approval.

Changshu 87

Minutes of the County Government Meeting: The county government of this county held its 25th county government meeting at 9:00 AM yesterday, chaired by County Magistrate Tan. Matters discussed: (1) The Executive Committee of the County Party Department requested that the provincial order to change the land tax from "liang" to "yuan" be implemented as soon as possible. The decision was to instruct the Finance Bureau to investigate the land tax situation in this county and begin preparations. The 12th district chief meeting was held at 2:00 PM in the afternoon, still chaired by County Magistrate Tan. Matters discussed: (1) Each district will abolish the baozhang (village head) system and establish township ding (local officers). The decision was passed. (2) Regarding the method of soliciting customs treasury bonds, the decision was that the amount should be based on the amount of land. The First District will solicit two-thirds, and the remaining fourteen districts will solicit one-third.

The Village and Li Council Received an Order to Stop Recruiting Soldiers: The Jiaxing County Government has received an order to stop recruiting soldiers. Therefore, it telegraphed the public security bureaus and district offices on the deletion day to inform them, and the education bureau to notify them. After receiving the telegram, the district offices telegraphed the village and li councils and township preparation offices on the milling day to stop recruiting soldiers.

Jiangyin 89

The Provincial Committee Secretly Investigated Important Cases in Cheng: Xiao Hanfan, the director of the Fifth Section of the Secretariat of the Provincial Government, and Wang Chan, came to Cheng together on the order of Chairman Ye the day before yesterday. They resided in the Central Hotel and kept their movements very secret. They were investigating a certain important case. They met with party and government organs on the 15th and 16th and returned to the province on the 17th.

The Public Security Bureau Investigated the Illegal Soil Seizure Case: Jiangyin is located at the mouth of the Yangtze River and has many ports and rivers, making it a hub for soil merchants. The day before yesterday, soil merchants Dai and Pu and others pooled funds to transport more than 1,400 taels of opium from Hankou. The opium had already been unloaded, and in the morning, it was divided into two packages and transferred to small boats at the Longxu River mouth for sale to various ports in Wuxi and Changzhou. Zhou Jintang (nicknamed "Little Cowhide"), a former squad member of a certain team, and seven or eight others seized the opium, implicating the former acting captain Wu. After the opium was divided, each person received about one catty. After the Public Security Bureau learned of this, Chief Inspector Cheng was dispatched on the morning of the 17th to arrest Zhou Jintang and take him to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Zhou did not admit to it and was released on bail, with instructions to investigate the people who seized the opium and report them to the bureau for verification.

A Secret Agent Was Dismembered by Bandits Yesterday: The bandit Lu Zhanglin in Anquancun, Sanguan Township, East Suburbs, has been acting lawlessly but has not been apprehended. The secret agent Dai Jinrong learned of his return home. He and Hu Longfei, the driver Wu Jintang (from Qingtingqiao, East Suburbs), went to Anquancun. They were lured by the bandits to the wilderness. The driver was shot dead in three places by a box cannon, and Dai Jinrong and Hu Longfei were dismembered into several pieces by the bandits. A relative of Lu Baoguang, a clerk of the county government, was collecting fish accounts there and witnessed the situation. He was so frightened that he collapsed and died at home. Dai's mother, Wang, has sued the county government to arrest the murderers to console the departed souls.

Bandits Attempted to Escape and Were Shot Dead: The Wu-Cheng Joint Defense Association learned that the bandits Xi Binggen and Wu Yongzhen were in the Sanhekou area. Cao Xiangfang, the head of the Fifth District Defense Corps, dispatched a team to arrest them. Earlier, a bandit named Zhang Shunsheng was captured at Zhangjiaqiao. He confessed to kidnapping the child of the Xie Fulim family in Tanglin and other cases. He was temporarily detained at the corps headquarters pending transfer to the county government for legal action. Zhang Shunsheng attempted to escape over the wall the day before yesterday morning and was shot dead by the corps members while pursuing him to the east of Shengang Street. The county government was notified yesterday, and Miao Jieshou, the head of the Fifth District, was commissioned to inspect the body.

Nantong 90

No News of the Hostages in the Luhong Gate Kidnapping Case: The Luhong Gate kidnapping case occurred on the night of the 16th, in which six men and women were kidnapped. The military police are searching for the hostages everywhere, but there is still no news of them. Telegrams have been sent to neighboring counties for assistance in the search.

Headquarters Restricts the Pacification of Bandit Gangs: The major bandit gangs in northern Jiangsu, such as Shen Guanxi's gang, were previously considered for pacification by the military authorities, and a request was submitted to the Commander-in-Chief for approval. The headquarters is now focusing on suppressing the bandit gangs in northern Jiangsu to eliminate abuses. The military police are currently suppressing the bandits in the Lvsi and Jugang areas.

The Plight of the Reclamation Areas along the Coast of Northern Jiangsu: The reclamation areas along the coast of northern Jiangsu in Sheyang County and Henan Province have been severely ravaged by Ma Yuren, who colluded with sea bandits. During the recent suppression by the Provincial Security Corps, the bandits shot and killed the tenant leaders of various districts and burned the houses to the ground when they retreated. They also abducted more than one hundred tenants. The cotton of various companies was looted by the bandits. The reclamation industry has suffered a major blow and is becoming increasingly difficult to sustain.

Strict Prohibition of Disturbances by Wounded Soldiers: The Thirty-first Rear Hospital currently has 480 wounded soldiers. Recently, wounded soldiers have frequently caused disturbances in the four townships. Local communities have requested Dean Cao to issue badges and the military and police authorities to strictly prohibit such activities in accordance with the orders of the headquarters.

Rugao 91

The Fengli Sea Bandits Harass Ju Town: The Fengli sea bandits have been defeated by the police district. It is now learned that the bandits retreated to the seaside of Ju Town on the 12th. The district defense corps went to defend and suppress them. They made contact with the bandits in the Yangjiaban Sanguang area and engaged in a fierce battle for a long time. The bandits were defeated and retreated. Several bandits were killed, one was captured alive, and two hostages were rescued. According to a sea scout report in the evening, fourteen more bandit ships came to the port, intending to attack Ju Town. After receiving the report, the district office urgently telegraphed Jugang for assistance and telegraphed the county government to report the emergency. The county government has now telegraphed the Shen detachment, which is suppressing the bandits in Feng, and the Jugang Defense Corps to respond at any time and track down the bandits. After receiving the telegram, the Jugang District Office dispatched the first detachment of the Defense Corps to defend and suppress them.

Yangzhou 92

The Director of the Rural Hospital Was Detained: Tian Yueqiu, the director of the Tianye Hospital in Nanliuxiang, was named by a suspect communist in the county court as having conspired with Tian. The presiding judge issued a warrant in court, ordering the police to arrest him. He was arrested at the time (the afternoon of the 16th) and sent to prison after a brief interrogation. As a result, all the patients in the hospital were greatly embarrassed.

Provincial Order to Stop Recruiting New Soldiers: County Magistrate Chen Nanxuan has now received a telegram from the province, ordering him to stop recruiting new soldiers. All new soldiers recruited and sent after the 20th of this month will not be accepted. Yesterday (the 16th), he specifically ordered the districts to comply.

Ningbo 93

The Director of the Naval Affairs Office Was Kidnapped: Mao Youlan, a native of Fujian, resided under the Huaihua tree on the north bank of Jiangbei in this city. He was appointed by the Ministry of the Navy as the director of the Xiangshan Office to manage the leasing of official naval land in Xiangshan Port. Every year, he went to Xiangshan Port to collect rent in the morning and evening during the rice harvest season and at the end of the year. On the 7th of this month, Mao went to the area to collect rent as usual because the early rice had already been harvested. He stayed at a friend's house there. Unexpectedly, on the evening of the 11th, more than a dozen pirates suddenly arrived, speaking in a mixture of Ningbo and Taizhou dialects. Each held a quick-firing gun and rushed in, taking Mao away without a trace. Mao's family only learned of the incident the day before yesterday. They went to Xiangshan to investigate and telegraphed the Shanghai office of the Ministry of the Navy to issue an order for rescue.

Extorting Money Under False Pretenses: Those Responsible Are Beaten with Military Sticks: Four people, Zhang Zhong, Cai Peiliang, Li Boyun, and Fu Dinghua, posing as recruiting officers, forcibly conscripted farmers in Lujiabu, Cixi a few days ago, extorting 30 yuan from each person for redemption. The deception was exposed, and the people there reported it to the county government. Zhang Zhong and the other three were arrested and sent to the Ningbo Command Headquarters. After interrogation, the suspects confessed. They were each beaten with dozens of military sticks and sent to prison for strict punishment.

Bandit Gangs Gathered in Fuzhu Ridge: Fuzhu Ridge in Fenghua is located in a remote area, with high mountains and ridges, and is adjacent to the three counties of Xinchang, Shengxian, and Ninghai. As a result, bandits often come and go there. Recently, it was learned that three gangs of bandits from the neighboring counties of Xinchang, Shengxian, and Ninghai, totaling about three to four hundred people, have gathered there. They have repeatedly committed arson and looting. After receiving the report yesterday, the Fenghua County Government sent the Defense Corps to suppress them and ordered the military and police in the city to strictly enforce martial law.

Anqing 94

The Provincial Government Reappoints the Magistrates of Seven Counties: At the regular meeting on the 14th, the Provincial Government passed the reappointment of the magistrates of seven counties, including Huaining. Ma Guangzong, the magistrate of Fuyang County, has not arrived at his post for a long time and should be recalled immediately. Wang Yunlong is appointed to act in his place. Fang Shaozhou, the magistrate of Dingyuan County, has not arrived at his post for a long time and should be recalled immediately. Wu Shusheng, the magistrate of Huaining County, is transferred to act in his place, and Wang Cuimin is appointed to act in the vacant post of Huaining County magistrate. Li Wan, the magistrate of Shucheng County, is to be recalled immediately. Wu Yunfeng is appointed to act in his place. Li Cishong, the magistrate of Tianchang County, is dismissed and investigated. Wu Shuxun is appointed to act in his place. Liu Xingwu, the magistrate of Langxi County, is transferred to the province. Sun Gongming, the magistrate of Wuhu County, is transferred to act in his place, and Yu Shangying is appointed to act in the vacant post of Wuhu County magistrate.

The Compilation of Provincial Chronicles is Actively Underway: The Provincial Government recently hired Jiang Wei, the former director of the Anhui Education Department, as the director of the Provincial Gazette Office and stipulated that 1% of the national and local taxes should be added as the office's expenses. The Ministry of Finance firmly refused to do so. The Provincial Reserve is considering planning. It was resolved at the recent 139th regular meeting to deliver the entire volume for review. Once the funds are available, it will proceed actively.

Zhejiang Local Education Personnel Training Method 98

The Zhejiang Education Department, on the order of the province, drafted ten articles of the training method for local education administrative personnel and submitted them to the provincial government for review. The instructions for approval have been received. The following is a transcript: (1) All personnel who pass the Zhejiang Provincial Local Education Administrative Personnel Examination must be trained separately by the Education Department in accordance with this method. (2) The training methods are divided into two types: A. Observation in the department; B. Sending to various places for inspection. (3) For personnel observing in the department, the director of the Education Department will assign practice in each section, and the section chiefs will be responsible for guidance. (4) For personnel sent to various places for inspection, the director of the Education Department will specify the scope and location for separate inspections. (5) The length of the training period will be determined separately by the director of the Education Department based on the experience and performance of each individual. (6) During the training period, the allowances and inspection travel expenses of the personnel will be provided by the Education Department at its discretion. (7) During the training period, each trainee should compile a detailed work report, together with the designated official documents, plans, regulations, etc., or inspection opinions, and submit them to the section chief for assessment at the end of the period, and the Education Department director will evaluate their performance. (8) After the training is completed, when there are vacancies for education administrative personnel, they will be assigned separately. (9) For personnel who have passed the examination and have been assigned before the promulgation of this method, the director of the Education Department will consider the situation and transfer them back to complete the training and assign someone to act on their behalf, or the director of the Education Department will assign practical matters of education administration for investigation and research, and order them to submit a report. After review and found satisfactory, the procedures for completing the training may be waived. (10) This method will be implemented after being submitted to and approved by the provincial government.

Jiangsu Universal Education Experimental Zone Plants Wheat for Experiment 99

The joint office for the preparation of compulsory education in various counties in Jiangsu, Universal Education Experimental Zone (Zhenjiang Zhongling New Village), began to experiment with improved agricultural products and signed a contract with Lu Yueting, a resident of the zone, to conduct a cooperative agricultural experiment station. Wheat was first planted for experiment. The best wheat seeds were selected from the wheat experiment station of the Provincial Education College at Outangqiao, Wuxi, and planted in the cooperative experiment station in the zone. The entire field was first divided into two areas, A and B. Area A was planted by the owner with the original wheat seeds of the zone using old methods. Area B was divided into a general cultivation area and a variety experiment area. The general area was divided into two types, planted with American white skin and Jinling University No. 26 seeds. The special area was divided into six types: (1) Zone planted with American white skin seeds, (2) Zone planted with Japanese red skin seeds, (3) Zone planted with Nanjing red shell seeds, (4) Zone planted with Jin Da No. 26 seeds, (5) Zone planted with Jiangdongmen seeds, (6) Zone planted with Wujin awnless seeds, all using strip sowing to test which variety is suitable for the soil in the zone. After the harvest next spring, the variety with the best results will be selected and introduced to the residents of the zone for planting.

Anhui University Faculty Salary Standards 100

▲ Drafted by the University Affairs Meeting

Anhui Provincial Anhui University held its second administrative meeting on the afternoon of the 8th, and passed the salary standards for faculty and staff, which are roughly as follows: The grades of faculty and staff salaries are determined based on academic qualifications and past performance. (1) Full-time professors are divided into five grades, teaching at least ten hours per week, which may be reduced for those concurrently holding administrative positions. Grade 1: 340, Grade 2: 320, Grade 3: 300, Grade 4: 280, Grade 5: 260. (2) Part-time professors are paid by the hour, with the standard being the level of the subject taught. Per hour: divided into three grades of five yuan, six yuan, and seven yuan. (3) Full-time lecturers are divided into five grades, teaching at least six hours per week, which may be reduced for those concurrently holding administrative positions. Grade 1: 220, Grade 2: 200, Grade 3: 180, Grade 4: 160, Grade 5: 140. (4) Part-time lecturers are paid by the hour, divided into three grades of four yuan, five yuan, and six yuan. (5) Teaching assistants are divided into three grades: 120, 100, 80. (6) Newly hired teachers, except for special appointments, will be paid from the date of appointment. (7) If a teacher asks someone to substitute for a class due to personal reasons, the salary will be paid by the substitute. (8) Secretaries, document clerks, and group leaders will continue to be paid according to the original standards. (9) Group members are divided into five grades: 80, 70, 60, 50, 40.

New Discoveries in the Modern Student Circle 107

▲ The Modern Student Published by Datong Bookstore

The Remote Causes and Recent Consequences of This Aborted Expedition (3) by Yu Hengzhi 115

Later, their deputy leader, Mr. Yu Juxian, published three reasons why South China refused to allow its players to participate. He said: (1) The organization is not transparent; (2) The procedures for contacting players are not proper; (3) The finances are not abundant. These three understandings seem very accurate, but in my opinion, they are all excuses. First, he said our organization is not transparent. I say our organization is too transparent, and our shortcoming lies in being too transparent. Because if we had consistently used the name Lehua and relied solely on Lehua's strength to deal with it, although the name would be too narrow and the strength weaker, we would not have relied on external parties and would have been smooth sailing and unhindered. If Mr. Yu says that the meaning of transparency is to push the matter to the Sanhua Association for joint management, then I feel it would be even more harmful, and the consequences would be even more unimaginable. This is because I have always known that the two Chinese associations in Hong Kong and China are incompatible. Usually, when Hong Kong and China encounter team selections for foreign affairs, many unnecessary disputes arise over the number of attendees. Such trivial matters have already occurred. How much noise would there be for an expedition? Second, he said that the procedures for contacting players were not proper. We followed the precedents. I remember that there wasn't even a single notice during the Australian tour. Although the players belonged to one association, if they were amateur athletes, they had the right to freedom, and the association could not control and manage them. Commercial procedures are a step to infringing on the rights of amateur players and polluting their personality. Moreover, South China has previously asked Lehua's Zhou, Chen, Dai, and Li to help them, but there has never been any verbal or written notice or consultation. If Lehua's procedures are improper, South China's procedures are even more unspeakable, Mr. Yu. The facts are obvious. I don't think you will have forgotten it. Third, he said that Lehua's finances were not abundant, which is even more nonsense. How did Mr. Yu know enough about our financial situation to dare to make such a judgment? As I said above, our expenses and deposits were sufficient to offset each other, and we were also careful to prepare for unexpected needs. How could we have risked going ahead without any idea? Mr. Yu is too much of a worrier. Forget it. Only you can know your own actions. I hope that everyone can treat each other with sincerity in the future and not use words to cover up because covering up is only temporary and ultimately does no good.

Many people are puzzled and looking for the following two answers: (1) Why doesn't the Hong Kong Association agree? (2) Why are the two Chinese associations unwilling to cooperate? Although I dare not be certain about the truth, I estimate it to be about eighty or ninety percent. The Hong Kong Association's annual income relies entirely on the Chinese team. If the Chinese team's masters leave, it will definitely affect its economic position. Recently, its means of ruling that Cao and others are not allowed to participate is to take a permanent solution and prohibit Chinese people from daring to try again in the future. As for the two Chinese associations, they want to take care of their own strength, so they have tried various ways to prevent their respective players from participating. In addition, mutual suspicion is also a major reason.

I think the purpose of the two Chinese associations is a big mistake. Because if you want your power to be strong, it is better to send a few people abroad to adopt better knowledge. Competing in Hong Kong all day long will result in very slow progress. The two Australian tours are enough to prove it. As for individual players, except for those who really cannot do it for factual reasons, it is worth traveling with the army no matter what. Those players who promised first and then broke their promises later, although I understand their position very well, I always think that it is a pity and foolish thing for an amateur player to give up his personal freedom and be bound by an association.

Finally, before I finish writing, I would also like to make a very simple explanation to Mr. Xu Zhendong. Mr. Xu has put in infinite thought for this expedition. I am very appreciative of his fairness and enthusiasm. However, there are many errors in what he published, and the facts are far from the topic. He said that the Hong Kong players did not participate because they were dissatisfied with the procedures. I am one of the initiators, so I should be more detailed. In fact, except for only one Hong Kong player who was not contacted because the demands were too harsh and exceeded amateur practice, all the others promised in person and were ready to participate. However, later, half were controlled by the association and half were incited by saboteurs, so they broke their promises at the last minute. As for what Mr. Xu said about insufficient funds and relying entirely on Java to raise the required funds, that is even more speculation. The facts I mentioned above are enough to defend me. I will not repeat them. We did not launch any donations in Nanyang twice, and although the results in Java were not as good this time, we were not blamed by the overseas Chinese. Although there were some complaints from gamblers who were temporarily angry, the vast majority knew our difficulties and forgave us, accounting for eighty or ninety percent. Mr. Xu also said that after we left, no one in the rear contacted the Shanghai General Association. I don't know what Mr. Xu knew that he said that. Before I left Shanghai, I personally entrusted Jiang Daozhang, Wang Fudan, and Wu Bangwei to organize the Lehua B team and participate as usual. However, later, because the expedition was stranded, we returned to Shanghai, and they gave up. In short, Mr. Xu's news is completely contrary to the facts. In order to avoid misunderstandings from the outside world and confusing the public, I hope that Mr. Xu will investigate the truth a little more when speaking in the future. If Mr. Xu still has anything unclear, I am also very happy to explain it in detail.

In the end, the rights and wrongs of the Chinese people can only be clarified among the Chinese people. It is better to mention less in English newspapers, because debating about the affairs of the Chinese people in English newspapers is not something we are optimistic about and willing to do. (The End)

All Circles Publicly Mourned President Tan Yesterday 118

▲ Ceremony of the Municipal Party Department

▲ Holding by Various Institutions

▲ Municipal Executive Committee The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department convened all party members yesterday to hold a public memorial ceremony for President Tan. The memorial hall was set up in the grand auditorium on the third floor of the department. A plain cloth banner was hung in the hall, which read, "Public Memorial Ceremony for President Tan." A portrait of President Tan was hung in the center, with the Party and National flags crossed on top. A long couplet on the side was presented by all the executive and supervisory members of the Party Department. The text read, "Great strategy to overcome difficulties, Mount Heng rises with clouds to benefit the world; great name passed down to the universe, the star of Shangtai falls and dims Jiangnan." A sacrificial table was set up in front of the statue, with several offerings placed on it and two bottles of fresh flowers. In addition, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works and the Municipal Women's Association and others sent wreaths, which were displayed in front of the statue. Various levels of Party departments also sent elegiac couplets. The entire hall was arranged in a solemn and respectful manner. Looking up at the portrait of President Tan, it still seemed as if he were alive, which made people stand in awe and respect. From 9:00 a.m., all the staff of the Party Department and the various district Party departments and district branches sent representatives to pay their respects one after another. Various institutions and organizations, such as the Municipal Government, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, the Telephone Bureau, the Municipal Bureau of Finance, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, the Municipal Bureau of Health, the Municipal Bureau of Port Affairs, the Telegraph Bureau, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, the Municipal Bureau of Public Security, the Municipal Bureau of Land, the Municipal Bureau of Education, the Municipal People's Association, the China Law Society, the Municipal Women's Association, the Jingwu Association, the Rongkang Workers' Association, the Nanhua Workers' Association, the Jianbu Workers' Association, the Commercial Press Labor Union, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Flannelette Labor Union, the China Merchants Bureau, the Arsenal, and the Tea and Snack Labor Union of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway also sent personnel to pay their respects until 4:00 p.m. It was said that representatives were still going to pay their respects.

▲ Naval Party Department The Naval Special Party Department, together with the Naval Reorganization Office and the Headquarters of the Training Fleet, held a public memorial service for the late Tan Yenkai, a member of the Central Committee, at 1:00 p.m. yesterday. Many representatives from the Party departments of various ships stationed in Shanghai and Party departments at all levels attended. Chen Xunyong, a standing committee member of the Special Party Department, presided over the ceremony, and Ren Guangyu reported on the deeds of the late Tan, a member of the Central Committee. The meeting adjourned at 2:00 p.m. after the ceremony.

▲ Lianglu Party Department The Special Party Department of the Beijing-Shanghai-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway held a public memorial ceremony for President Tan in the auditorium of the Party Department at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. Min Luoping presided over the meeting, and the ceremony was performed as usual. After the chairman finished his report, Chen Pin, Zhou Lianze, and Wang Ren spoke one after another (the words were not recorded at length). The meeting adjourned after the ceremony.

▲ County-Affiliated Institutions The county-affiliated institutions held a public memorial ceremony for Mr. Tan Zu'an in the county government auditorium at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. All personnel from the County Reorganization Committee, the County Government, and its affiliated bureaus attended. County Chief Yan presided over the ceremony, Lü Zhe was the master of ceremonies, and Jiang Yanchou reported. The meeting adjourned after the ceremony in the afternoon.

▲ Municipal Chamber of Commerce Memorial Oration The 16th Standing Committee meeting of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce resolved to publicly elect Chairman Wang Xiaolai and standing committee members Ye Huijun and Wang Yansong as representatives to publicly mourn the late President Tan. It is reported that the three representatives have already gone to Beijing last night to prepare to participate in the public memorial service of the mass organizations of various provinces and cities on the afternoon of the 19th. The Chamber of Commerce has also prepared a special memorial oration as follows: On the 22nd day of the 9th month of the 19th year of the Republic of China, Tan Zu'an, President of the Executive Yuan of Chaling, died in office. The whole country was shocked and mourned. On the 19th day of the 10th month of that year, all party and government agencies and mass organizations inside and outside Beijing held a public memorial service in Central Park. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully follows the mass organizations and publicly elects Chairman Wang Xiaolai and standing committee members Wang Yansong and Ye Huijun to attend the memorial service and to express our feelings in the following words: Alas, riding a carp to heaven, the spirit returns to Jiuyi; with labor to secure the country, a hundred generations of ancestral shrines are revered. Recalling the Xinhai Revolution, when Wuchang raised its troops, the disparity in numbers and the difference in strength made the situation precarious. The turtle mountain garrison was lost, and the defense line was suddenly withdrawn. A corner of the country resisted the enemy, and the overall situation was in imminent danger. Hunan and Hubei, like lips and teeth, raised the flag of righteousness, providing funds and shoes in a timely manner. The morale of the army was strengthened, and the enemy's courage was shattered. Continuing the existence and preserving the inheritance, who else but you, sir? The political situation of the world is changing and unpredictable. Only your integrity, sir, has been followed by the Party and the country. The rugged roads of Hunan and Guangdong have remained unchanged through ten thousand changes. Strong warlords have surrendered, and cunning bandits have fled. The stability of the Lingnan region has been established, and the foundation for unification has been laid. With your elegance, sir, you have relied on your integrity to direct and command. The Jiangnan region has been pacified, and a great contribution has been made. The multitudes are looking forward to peace. You, sir, have been in charge of the Executive Yuan, determined to clarify matters, providing relief and gathering the people to comfort the common people. China has been disturbed again, and fierce generals have claimed troops. You, sir, have used your reputation to sit in the capital, providing uninterrupted transportation, and thus pacifying You and Bing. The day of triumph is coming, and construction is just beginning. Relying on you, sir, for the wisdom of Fang Xuanling and Du Ruhui to manage and plan. Why does heaven not pity us? A great star has suddenly fallen. The country has lost its pillar, and the Party has lost its loyal servant. Raising a glass in mourning, our tears and sobs are unanimous. May you enjoy this sacrifice.

▲ Japanese Representative Goes to Beijing Mr. Shigemitsu Aoi, the Japanese Acting Minister to China, received a telegram from the Japanese government yesterday, instructing him to represent the Japanese government in participating in the state funeral of the late President Tan. After receiving the order, Shigemitsu left for Beijing on the night express at 11:00 p.m. yesterday. Du Xigui Returned to China Yesterday 119

▲ Opinions on the Naval Examination of Various Countries

▲ Report is Currently Being Organized

▲ Entering Beijing to Meet Chairman Chiang Within Days

Du Xigui, the Special Envoy of the Navy, a naval admiral, who inspected the navies of Europe, the United States, and Japan, returned to China with his secretary and entourage. He left Shanghai on November 10 last year and traveled around the world. His secretary-general, Dong Xianguang, returned to China in May of this year. Du rested in France. On the 18th of last month, Du and his entourage, Huang Xianqi, Chief of Staff of the Mazu Fortress Command, returned home from Marseille on the Japanese ship Terukuni Maru. At 8:30 a.m. yesterday, they arrived at the Huishan Wharf. Naval dignitaries and commanders of various ships gathered at the wharf around 7:00 a.m. to welcome them. Among them were Li Dingxin, the former Minister of the Navy, Gan Lian'ao, the former Commander of the Training Fleet, Chen Xunyong, the current Commander of the Naval Training Fleet, Ren Guangyu, Director of the Military Affairs Bureau, Shen Deshe, Director of the Aircraft Factory, Wu Zhennan, Director of the Coastal Defense Office, Ma Deji, Director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, Wu Guangzong, Director of the Survey Bureau, and Dong Xianguang, totaling more than a hundred people. After Du and others landed, they took a car to his private residence to rest.

▲ Du's Talk Our reporter interviewed Du Xigui on the ship yesterday morning. Du was full of energy and had a friendly smile. He spoke in detail about the experience of inspecting the navies of various countries and his opinions on future construction. At 4:00 p.m. yesterday, Du hosted reporters at the Naval Social Club at a welcome tea party. The following is a summary of what Du said yesterday, outlining the main points. Du said, "I left Shanghai on November 10 last year and have been away for nearly a year. In June of this year, in Paris, the car we were riding in was hit hard by a freight car, and I was hospitalized for almost three months due to injuries. Therefore, the actual inspection time was only seven months. The competition among the navies of various countries is fierce today, and each country has its own strengths. England, established as an island nation, has the most complete and well-organized navy due to its environment, and it can be called the sole hegemon. Secondly, Japan's perseverance and hard work in managing the navy for thirty years has already become a great sight to behold. Then, the United States is known for its wealth, France is known for its aviation industry, and Italy's naval schools focus on horsemanship. Although Germany is oppressed by various countries and its armaments are restricted, its navy is gradually recovering and is able to change its policies. The whole country, from top to bottom, advocates sports, and even laborers are forced to join sports associations to temper their martial spirit and create their qualifications as a military nation. Its perseverance is truly admirable. Seeing the surge in maritime power, the powers have limited it through the London Naval Treaty, but the result has failed to fully satisfy people. Recently, the competition between France and Italy has been particularly fierce, and its effects can be seen at a glance."

A photograph of the Naval Social Club welcoming Du Xigui (taken by Zhonghua Photography). The right corner shows a photograph of Du arriving in Shanghai (taken by this museum).

▲ Naval Construction As for our country's navy, it is extremely young and cannot be compared with Europe, the United States, and Japan. Even in terms of the future construction of our country's navy, it is by no means a local issue. It is not easy to succeed until the national political economy and other matters are evenly developed. Naval construction requires a lot of money, and it is by no means possible to buy a few ships with hundreds of thousands of dollars. Therefore, if there is no sufficient financial guarantee and there is a continuous source, then is it better to dig meat to mend sores? Therefore, the first priority should be political prosperity, and then financial prosperity, before we can talk about the true construction of the navy. In terms of the current situation of China's naval construction, if we can move forward and not retreat in the future, then it will take another ten years to achieve great success. Several British and Japanese naval instructors have now been hired to come to China to develop naval education.

▲ Organize the Report Du also said, "I plan to compile a large book of reports based on what I have learned from this inspection. Dong Xianguang will compile and organize it, and it can be printed and published in about two or three months. Regarding my opinions on the current rectification of the Chinese navy, I have divided them into three strategies: upper, middle, and lower. I respectfully prepare for the National Government to adopt them. Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan will come to Shanghai from Beijing tonight because he is participating in the public memorial service for President Tan. After I meet with him, I will go to Beijing immediately to meet Chairman Chiang and report everything that has happened." Du was quite sharp in his remarks and spoke eloquently. He paid particular attention to the promotion of public sports. What is recorded now is only a tenth of it.

▲ Welcome Tea Party At 3:30 p.m. yesterday, more than a hundred people from the naval community in this city, famous people from Fujian Province in Shanghai, and relatives of Du gathered at the Naval Social Club on Ma Hoke Road to hold a grand tea party to welcome him. First, Major General Gan Lian'ao gave a welcome speech on behalf of Admiral Li Dingxin, in which he briefly stated, "General Du was sent to Japan and various countries in Europe and America last year by order of the National Government to inspect the naval situation and aviation affairs. It has been a year since he went abroad. What he has learned from this inspection will definitely make a great contribution to our country's naval community in the future."

▲ Main Points of the Reply Then, Du replied, briefly saying, "Brothers were sent to Japan and various countries in Europe and America last October by order of the National Government to inspect the navy. I am grateful for the send-off from all of you. Today, when I return home, I am grateful for the welcome from all of you present. I express my sincere gratitude and thank you for your kindness. What I have learned from my travels to Japan and various countries in Europe and America has been compiled into a book by Secretary Dong Xianguang and others. Today, I would like to report to you my impressions of what I have learned from the inspection. I studied in Europe for five years and graduated with considerable results. Now, science is flourishing, and research and academics are becoming more and more difficult. Students from various countries entering naval schools must graduate from middle school and then undergo years of specialized study before they can get a glimpse of the doorway. Many university graduates and graduates of general schools also join the navy and receive in-depth training, so talents emerge in large numbers. In recent years, our country has been plagued by internal strife, and the government has had no time to take care of the navy, which is a great pity. Now, if we want to reorganize the navy, the first thing we must do is raise sufficient funds, and the second is to cultivate talents. Talents and economy cannot be neglected. Although the government has sent naval officers and students to study abroad, the number is very small, and even if they return to the country after graduation, it is difficult to be effective. Therefore, brothers advocate that we hope that the government will set up more naval schools, recruit naval professionals, hire foreign professors, and proceed step by step, so that we can achieve good results in the future. In short, the country should not rely entirely on armaments. Even if there is a very powerful and very strong army and navy, if the opinions of all parties are divided, the strength will be weakened. The failure of various undertakings is also due to selfishness. People in the army and navy only know about their own interests and do not know about the country's army and navy. Therefore, the strength of the army and navy can only be seen to be scattered and declining, and cannot be concentrated and strengthened. The capacity of the Chinese people is too narrow, and their jealousy is too heavy. As a result, all things fail. Therefore, when it comes to construction, the first step is to transform the selfish mentality of the people, so that the majority can take care of the interests of the public, and then unite and cooperate to build a new China. It is not only the development of the navy that is involved." At about 5:00 p.m., they took photos and dispersed happily.
