The Transport Association Telegraphed to Request the Release of Vehicles 121

Recently, the various transit companies of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway have been extremely crowded with passengers and goods, and the goods piled up at the various stations such as the Maigen Road Station in Shanghai are like mountains, all because the Railway Bureau lacks vehicles and cannot load them. Various merchants have urged the various carriers to speed up the loading and transportation of the goods to avoid long delays and losses. Therefore, the various companies convened their colleagues at the Transport Company to discuss remedial measures and resolved to telegraph General Commander Chiang, ordering him to quickly release the military vehicles that had been detained for transportation, so as to avoid commercial difficulties. The original telegram from the Association to General Commander Chiang is recorded below: Nanjing, General Commander Chiang, please be informed that the various companies of the same industry have stated that Shanghai Station has recently accumulated 2,800 tons of goods, which cannot be delivered due to the lack of vehicles. All the vehicles at the various stations have been detained in Nanjing with military supplies, about a hundred vehicles in total, stored in the vehicles as warehouses without unloading, etc. It is reported that military affairs are being pacified, and all industries are in the process of importing and transporting goods and starting business. It is difficult to obstruct and detain vehicles. Military use is important, but people's livelihood should also be taken into account. I respectfully request that you telegraph your subordinates, ordering that all loaded trains be unloaded as soon as they arrive, and order the Railway Bureau to quickly return the empty vehicles to the various stations with goods to meet the transportation needs and take care of people's livelihood. It is hoped that this will be implemented and will be a great blessing. Shanghai Municipal Transportation Association respectfully kowtows.

Notice of Deferred Payment of Water Rates from the Taxpayers' Association 122

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association, regarding the uncompleted audit of the Shanghai Municipal Council's water supply, issued a notice yesterday to all sectors about deferring water rate payments. The letter reads as follows: "To all tenants in the Shanghai International Settlement: The water rate has traditionally been calculated at 60% of the house rent, mostly included in the rent by the landlord. This time, the Shanghai Waterworks Company has arbitrarily increased the price by a quarter compared to before. Our association has strongly protested based on reason, and the Chinese directors have striven to argue the case. The company, knowing that public opinion is not to be defied and that legal grounds are lacking, has automatically accepted the instructions of the Public Works Department, inviting representatives from our association and the Real Estate Association to conduct an audit. Our association immediately declared to the company that, before the audit results are available and a price increase is deemed necessary, the water rate should legally be collected at the original rate (i.e., 6% of the rent). If a price increase is later deemed necessary, it will be collected retroactively, etc. The Shanghai Real Estate Association has also published the above information in newspapers. Unexpectedly, it has been found that the Laou Kai Mow & Co. rent collection agency, in its notice to the residents of the De'an Lane property managed for Zhu Yicai, stated: 'The Shanghai Waterworks Company of the Public Concession has decided to increase the water surcharge by 25%, which is 15% for tenants, starting from September 1, 1930. Our agency will also collect this amount according to the conditions stated on the rent receipt. Therefore, starting from September 1930, an additional water fee of 25% will be collected with the rent, i.e., 2 fen 5 li per tael of rent. If the water company increases or decreases the rate in the future, our agency will also increase or decrease it accordingly. In addition to stamping the rent receipt as proof, this notice is specially issued for your information.' Zhu Yicai is the son of the late business leader Zhu Lanfang. At a time when all residents are opposing the water rate increase, he should not take advantage of the water company's price increase by accepting the increase on one hand and collecting an extra 1% of the rent on the other. We believe that this is the agency's own decision. In addition to writing to Mr. Zhu to correct this, we are concerned that other landlords or rent collection agencies may be taking similar actions. Therefore, we are issuing this special notice to tenants in the settlement, urging everyone to refuse to pay the increased water rate or any other exploitative charges during this audit period. This matter concerns the interests of all residents in terms of water usage. Please do not misunderstand. We hope you will all take note."

▲Letter to Laou Kai Mow & Co.: "To the esteemed managers: According to the notice received by the tenants of De'an Lane from your company, 'The Shanghai Waterworks Company of the Public Concession has decided to increase the water surcharge by 25%, which is 15% of the rent, starting from September 1, 1930. Our agency will also collect this amount according to the conditions stated on the rent receipt. Therefore, starting from September 1930, an additional water fee of 25% will be collected with the rent, i.e., 2 fen 5 li per tael of rent. If the water company increases or decreases the rate in the future, our agency will also increase or decrease it accordingly. In addition to stamping the rent receipt as proof, this notice is specially issued for your information.' The De'an Lane property belongs to Zhu Yicai. At a time when we are opposing the arbitrary water rate increase, was this notice issued by your company with Mr. Zhu's written authorization, or was it your own decision? Please provide a clear answer. As for taking the opportunity to collect an extra tael per hundred taels of rent as an unexpected profit, this is not the time to comment, and we will not inquire about it for now. We hope you will investigate and provide a prompt and clear reply."

▲Letter to Zhu Yicai: "We have received a notice from the tenants of De'an Lane, managed by your rental agent, Laou Kai Mow & Co., which states (details omitted). Regarding the Shanghai Waterworks Company's price increase, all residents have risen up in opposition. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce has been returning water bills, and the Shanghai Real Estate Association has repeatedly published notices stating that before the audit results are available and a price increase is deemed necessary, the water rate should be paid at the original price (i.e., 6% of the rent). The efforts made by our association and the Chinese directors have been widely reported in the local newspapers. You are undoubtedly well aware of this. We know that you have a fair and just heart and are willing to share with others. This kind of disregard for public opinion in accepting the water rate increase and collecting an extra 1% of the rent is likely not your intention but rather your rental agent's own decision to curry favor with the water company and to further curry favor with you by obtaining an extra 1% profit. The rental agent certainly gains in two ways, but your good reputation will inevitably suffer as a result. This matter concerns the interests of the public, and you cannot afford to ignore it. We hereby request that you promptly stop this absurd action and order the return of any money that has already been collected to avoid arousing public anger. We hope you will understand."

▲Letter to the Real Estate Association: "To the esteemed managers: We recently received a notice from the tenants of De'an Lane, managed by the Laou Kai Mow & Co. rental agency, which states, 'The Shanghai Waterworks Company of the Public Concession has decided to increase the water surcharge by 25%, which is 15% of the rent, starting from September 1, 1930. Our agency will also collect this amount according to the conditions stated on the rent receipt. Therefore, starting from September 1930, an additional water fee of 25% will be collected with the rent, i.e., 2 fen 5 li per tael of rent. If the water company increases or decreases the rate in the future, our agency will also increase or decrease it accordingly. In addition to stamping the rent receipt as proof, this notice is specially issued for your information.' Your association has made great efforts to oppose this arbitrary water rate increase, showing that your industry does not take advantage of the water rate increase to raise rents, which is greatly admired by the public. However, at a time when your association has published notices stating that the water rate should be paid at the original price, we have discovered this acceptance of the water rate increase and the exploitation of collecting an extra 1% of the rent, which is a disgrace to your industry. Furthermore, the De'an Lane property belongs to Zhu Yicai, the son of the late businessman Zhu Lanfang. This action is likely not Mr. Zhu's intention but rather the rental agent's own decision. You should take immediate steps to correct this internationally embarrassing behavior to protect the interests of the residents."

Pan Gongzhan's Talk on the National Salvation Fund 125

▲Already Handling Labor Affairs in Accordance with the Central Government's Intentions

Yesterday, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited Pan Gongzhan, a standing committee member of the Municipal Party Committee, to inquire about the progress of the former Anti-Japanese Association's National Salvation Fund. Mr. Pan replied, "When the Anti-Japanese Association ended and was reorganized into the National Salvation Association the year before last, the collection of the National Salvation Fund for inferior goods was immediately stopped. According to the report of the National Salvation Fund Custody Committee, the total amount of collected and deposited funds was 108,000 taels of standard silver, 115,000 silver dollars, and 110,060 two-five treasury bonds issued by the Jianghai Customs, totaling approximately 380,000 yuan. At that time, the funds were deposited in the silver and money industry, preparing to establish national goods factories and national goods companies. Later, the Central Government designated the funds for labor hygiene and labor education purposes. Therefore, the National Salvation Association, at the time of its dissolution, reported the funds to the Municipal Party Committee for verification. The Municipal Party Committee, in accordance with the Central Government's intentions, decided to allocate all the funds separately to the Financial Committee of the Labor Hospital and the Financial Committee of Labor Education for safekeeping to carry out these two projects. These two financial committees are composed of members selected by the Municipal Party Committee from various sectors of the Party, government, business, and education in this city. All procedures are conducted using a collegial system, so there should be no breach of trust. The Shanghai Labor Hospital has already purchased land and buildings on Xiaoshadu Road in West Shanghai and has been operating for more than a year, providing treatment to 300 to 400 patients daily. The monthly expenses, in addition to relying on interest from the fund, are still insufficient, and the financial committee is responsible for raising funds. The Municipal Party Committee has also appointed committee members to plan labor education projects, intending to establish compulsory labor schools in various districts within the possible scope of the fund's interest. As for the fine yarn factory fund collected on behalf of the Anti-Japanese Association, it is said that fine yarn is a raw material for cloth and sock factories. According to regulations, it could have been exempt from the National Salvation Fund. However, at that time, citizens, recognizing that there were no fine yarn products in the country, collected the fine yarn factory fund at the request of the dyeing and weaving industry, and the dyeing and weaving industry issued receipts for special storage, designated for the purpose of establishing a fine yarn factory, and not as ordinary national salvation funds. When the National Salvation Association was reorganized, the collection of this fine yarn fund was also stopped. The total amount collected was probably between 500,000 taels. Representatives from the Jiangsu and Zhejiang cotton weaving industry associations and the Anti-Japanese Association jointly appointed a custody committee to be responsible for safekeeping. Later, the Jiesheng Yarn Factory Preparatory Committee was organized, notifying all factories that had paid the fine yarn factory fund to exchange their fund receipts for Jiesheng Yarn Factory stock receipts, and to organize a joint-stock limited company according to law. This method was reported to the Municipal Party Committee for record. However, the fine yarn factory fund was kept by the Jiesheng Yarn Factory Preparatory Committee and was not submitted to the Municipal Party Committee for transfer. Therefore, it is not an ordinary national salvation fund and is different from public funds in nature. It is reported that the yarn factory has already convened an inaugural meeting, elected directors, and purchased factory land and machinery. The factory buildings are also under construction. They are currently preparing documents to submit to the Bureau of Social Affairs and forward to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval to register the company."

Negotiations on the Shanghai Municipal Council's Cross-Border Bridge Repair 131

▲Dispatching Armed Chinese Police to Guard Day and Night

▲Requesting Serious Negotiations to Argue the Case

The Chengjiaqiao Bridge on Hongqiao Road in West Shanghai, built by the British Shanghai Municipal Council across the border, connects to Sheshan Road and reaches the airport. Recently, the bridge has been in disrepair for many years, and the British Shanghai Municipal Council has dispatched two armed Chinese police officers to guard it day and night. All heavy vehicles are prohibited from passing, so buses are turning around at Chengjiaqiao, which is inconvenient for passengers and greatly affects the company's business. Unexpectedly, it has been nearly twenty days since the dispatch of the police, and no repairs have been started. Wang, the head of the 1st Branch of the 6th District in charge of the area, learned that the land of Chengjiaqiao belongs to the Chinese area, and foreigners should not overstep their authority. Therefore, Wang seriously negotiated with the Jing'an Temple Police Station the other day to withdraw the Chinese police to avoid misunderstandings. At the same time, he reported the details to the Municipal Public Security Bureau and forwarded them to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to argue the case and protect sovereignty.

Hankou Cotton Merchants Petition in Beijing 132

▲Cotton Industry Representatives Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

▲Going to Beijing within Days to Request Relief

The cotton industry in Hankou has always been considered important. The cotton-producing areas along the Xiangjiang River and the Yangtze River in Hubei, and Changde and other places in Hunan, all belong to cotton-producing areas. The cotton industry in the port is divided into three groups: the Hankou Cotton Industry Association, which is a group that transports goods to Hankou from various places for sale; the Hankou Cotton Export Merchants Association, which is a group that purchases goods in Hankou and transports them to Shanghai; and the Cotton Industry Guild, which is an intermediary group for buyers and sellers. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce believed that Hankou's cotton industry was at the national hub, so it established the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau last year and appointed Xi Jian, Director of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, as the Director of the Bureau. Since the establishment of the Bureau, the cotton inspection has only conducted export inspections and has not conducted import inspections. The standard for humidity is set at 14%. Cotton that does not meet the standard is not allowed to be declared. The unqualified cotton must be re-inspected every three days, regardless of whether it is sunny or cloudy. The certificate is only limited to exports. If the goods arrive in Shanghai, they must still be re-inspected. The cotton merchants believe that due to the climate and geological conditions of Hankou, this standard is impossible to meet except in summer, and not inspecting imports and only inspecting exports makes it very inconvenient for exporters. Moreover, exporters originally use remittances as a tool to circulate funds, but if goods are detained for ten days, then turnover is not flexible, and business suffers even more. This summer, the cotton merchants submitted a report to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce requesting relief. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce sent personnel to Hankou to thoroughly investigate. Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry and Commerce, also instructed the Director of the Bureau to get close to merchants and not to allow policies that benefit merchants to harm merchants instead. However, since autumn, this major inspection issue has not been effectively resolved, so representatives have been selected to go to Beijing to petition the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to maintain the merchants' difficulties. The representatives arrived in Shanghai yesterday (17th) from Hankou and plan to discuss solutions with cotton industry colleagues in Shanghai within days and then go to Beijing to meet with the Minister of Industry and Commerce to request instructions from the Bureau to exchange inspection methods to provide relief.

This order must be obeyed."

Zhou Changshan Kidnapped 135

▲Kidnapped En Route to Jiangwan Racecourse

▲Bandits Fired Shots, Damaging Vehicle Tire

Zhou Changshan, son of Zhou Xiangyun from Ningbo County, residing at 27 Niuzhuang Road, was kidnapped by bandits at around 6:15 AM yesterday on the west side of the Jiangwan Sports Association. His private car's tires were damaged by gunfire from the bandits. The 5th Precinct, 5th Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau was notified of the incident approximately two hours after it occurred and dispatched detectives to investigate, but nothing has been found yet.

▲Kidnapped En Route: Zhou Changshan enjoys riding horses and keeps several horses at the Jiangwan Racecourse. He often goes riding there every morning when he has time. Yesterday morning, Zhou invited a riding instructor named Wachaliw, residing at 74 Dixiwei Road, to go to Jiangwan together. The chauffeur, Chen A'ming, drove them in car number 8334. As they drove north of the Hechang Oil Factory on the west side of the Sports Association, a car suddenly blocked their way in the middle of the road, stopping Zhou's car from proceeding. It was discovered that the car in front was driven by the kidnappers. Five men suddenly got out of the car. Three of them were armed with handguns and dragged Zhou and the chauffeur, Chen A'ming, out of the car and onto the kidnappers' car.

▲Bandits Open Fire: When kidnapping Zhou Changshan, the bandits fired two shots, damaging Zhou's car's tires. They then put paper-covered glasses on the faces of both master and servant and drove off towards Jiangwan at full speed. Near Zhizhi University, the bandits stopped the car and drove the chauffeur out. Before leaving, they gave him a letter to take to Zhou's family, stating that Zhou was now in the city and that they should rest assured. Wachaliw, the Westerner who was in the car with Zhou, waited for more than ten minutes before the chauffeur, Chen A'ming, ran back to the original location, changed the tire, and then drove back to Shanghai.

▲Reporting to the Police to Arrest the Bandits: The Westerner and the chauffeur went to the Dixiwei Police Station in the concession to report the incident. The police station said that the incident occurred in the Chinese area and forwarded it to the Qujiaqiao Police Station of the 5th District Public Security Bureau. The police station notified the Jiangwan 5th Precinct, 5th Section Public Security Bureau. By this time, two hours had passed since the incident. After receiving the information, Section Chief Dai ordered detectives to investigate, but the bandits had already fled far away and there were no clues. However, it was reported that the car used by the bandits seemed to be number 4120. Zhou Changshan, who was kidnapped, is 30 years old and enjoys sports. In addition to practicing martial arts, he also serves in the Shanghai Volunteer Corps. His father, Xiangyun, has always been engaged in real estate and is well known.

Suicide of a Corps Member Under the Oppression of Life 136

▲ Long Unemployed, Without Any Income

▲ How Can the Whole Family, Old and Young, Survive?

▲ Left with No Choice But to Resort to This Desperate Measure

Following the suicide case in which Wei Yanchang from Hunan and his entire family threw themselves into the Huangpu River due to environmental pressure, it has attracted considerable attention from the public. Unexpectedly, at 8:30 PM the night before last, another young man committed suicide by gunshot on Baoshan Road in Zhabei. The reason for his action was similar to Wei's. The deceased was You Jiaxiang, a member of the 3rd Team of the Shanghai North District Defense Corps, originally from Jiangxi. The situation was extremely tragic. The detailed account of the incident is described as follows:

▲ Family Circumstances: Corps Member You was 38 years old, originally from Jiangxi. He had resided in Shanghai for many years. His parents had passed away early. Currently, his family consists of a stepmother, his wife, Shi, who is 31 years old, and three children: a daughter, Jiazhen, 12 years old; a son, Guanlong, 8 years old; and a younger daughter, Sanyuan, who is just one year old. The entire family lived together at No. 50, Lane 4, Hengyu Lane, Qingyun Road, Zhabei.

▲ Unemployment Experience: Mr. You was an alumnus of Jinling University. He was extremely proud but also very kind and full of ambition. He once worked as a customs broker at Rendek Foreign Firm, and later joined Dachang Trading Company, also as a customs broker. He was known for his competence and was highly praised by his peers. However, when Dachang Trading Company declared bankruptcy due to poor business, Mr. You became unemployed. It wasn't until the spring of last year that he was introduced by a friend to the former Shanghai Baoshan County Defense Corps, 1st Regiment, 4th Team, now reorganized as the Shanghai North District Defense Corps, 3rd Team, at No. 1 Baoshan Lane, Baoshan Road, Zhabei, as a clerk.

▲ Hardships of Life: Mr. You had been unemployed for over a year. With several family members, living expenses only increased, and there was no reliable source of income. Moreover, the position as a corps member of the Defense Corps was completely voluntary. Not only was there no salary, but all transportation expenses had to be borne by himself. As a result, he was struggling to make ends meet. As the suffering deepened, he developed suicidal thoughts. A pessimistic attitude was often expressed. Although he had been repeatedly persuaded by friends, Mr. You had already made up his mind to die.

▲ Attempted Suicide: The tragic scene after You Jiaxiang's death on the evening of the 13th day of the eighth month of the lunar calendar this year.

Around 9 PM, he was at home chatting with his wife. Reaching a point of great sadness, You suddenly drew a pistol, intending to kill himself. Fortunately, his wife was quick and managed to snatch the gun away. She immediately ran to inform his close friend and fellow corps member, Bu Li Jing (Mr. You was introduced to the team by Mr. Bu), asking him to strongly advise him. You only lowered his head and said nothing, seemingly having realized his error slightly.

▲ Indeed, a Tragic Death: At 7:30 PM the night before last, You suddenly went to the team alone. He went directly to the room on the upper floor over the street to read the newspaper. All the personnel in the team had already left except for one person guarding the door downstairs in the side room. At 8:15 PM, a gunshot was suddenly heard from upstairs. Realizing something was wrong, the guard immediately went upstairs to investigate. He saw You sitting upright in a chair, his head tilted to the left, holding a revolver in his right hand, blood streaming from the left side of his chest near the nipple. Knowing it was suicide, he immediately reported to Team Leader Mo Huiqing and Deputy Team Leader Zhu Chucheng, who immediately gathered all the corps members to discuss the matter.

▲ Two Cards: Team Leader Mo also reported to the 5th District Headquarters next door and notified You's family. District Head You of the 5th District personally inspected the scene, ordered the local bailiff to report to the court for an autopsy, and found two of Mr. You's personal cards on the newspaper reading desk. One was addressed to his wife, which read, "Dear wife, we have endured hardship together for half a lifetime. I am truly sorry to you." The other was addressed to the colleagues in the team, which read, "Please take care of the funeral arrangements after my death. My family is poor and unable. Team leader, squad leader, and all comrades."

▲ Funeral Tomorrow: At 11:30 AM yesterday, a prosecutor specially dispatched by the court arrived at the team to conduct an autopsy. They found that the bullet had entered the left chest but did not exit. They immediately filled out the death certificate. The funeral was held at 2 PM in the afternoon. The team also issued a notice, the original text of which is recorded as follows: "Notice: Corps member You Jiaxiang of this team committed suicide with a revolver on the upper floor of the team headquarters at 8:15 PM last night. According to his family, this was due to the difficulties of life in modern society and the economic pressure of the environment. Mr. You was very enthusiastic about serving society during his lifetime and was especially diligent towards this team. His performance in defense operations was admired by his peers. Now, he has committed suicide due to the suffering of economic hardship. In addition to our grief, we, his comrades, will come to offer our condolences and escort him to his final resting place, fulfilling the duty of comradeship. It is hereby determined to hold the funeral at this team at 2:30 PM this afternoon. Special notice is given to all members to assemble at the team headquarters fully armed at 2 PM to depart for the funeral. Special notice." At the same time, a notice was issued at the entrance of Hengyu Lane, Qingyun Road, by neighbors Wang Shuwen, Wang Guizhang, Lu Yuxiang, and Zhao Yaowu, expressing their condolences for Mr. You's suicide due to economic pressure and requesting the public to find ways to help Mr. You's family. The words were extremely sad and sorrowful. However, some people said that You spent lavishly and owed more than two thousand taels of silver, and recently committed this desperate act due to the pressure from creditors. However, these are all speculative words due to nervous overreaction. The reason for this misunderstanding is that he liked to wear Western-style clothes when he was alive. As for You's debts, it may be the case, but the amount is no more than one hundred taels of silver.

Russian Child Missing for 49 Days Returns Safe and Sound 137

▲ Roaming the Countryside Like a Beggar

▲ Kind-Hearted Boatman Brings Him Back to Shanghai

▲ Mother Almost Thought She Was Meeting Him in a Dream

On August 30th, an eight-year-old Russian child, Vladimir, left home with his belongings, intending to go to Qingdao with two young companions by boat. Two days later, the two companions returned home, but the Russian child, who considered himself the first mate, had disappeared without a trace. It was rumored that he had drowned. His widowed mother, Mrs. Rokumsji, with only this one son, was deeply saddened by his disappearance and spent her days and nights in tears. But at 11:30 AM the day before yesterday, Mrs. Rokumsji went out to buy groceries and returned to suddenly find her beloved son, whom she could never forget in her dreams, soundly asleep in a sofa chair. She was initially surprised, thinking it was a dream, and rushed to touch him. It was indeed her son. She quickly took him into her arms and couldn't help but cry with joy. The child was also awakened and cried out upon seeing his mother. Thus, the mother and son, who had been separated for more than forty days, joyfully reunited, and the eight-year-old first mate, with the ambition to swallow rivers and seas, regained the joy of family life. It is said that after being abandoned by his two companions on the riverbank, the child wandered in the villages near Wusong, begging for food to survive. Before long, his clothes were tattered and barely covered his body, so the villagers gave him old clothes. Recently, he was brought back to Shanghai by a kind-hearted boatman, which allowed him to return home.

Two Tragic Accidents in the Huangpu River the Day Before Yesterday 138

▲ Swiss Man Falls into the River While Drowsing

▲ French Sailor Kicks Boatman into the River, Causing Him to Drown

The Shanghai Times reported that yesterday (17th) morning, two tragic accidents occurred in the Huangpu River within ten minutes of each other, and the locations of the accidents were less than a cable's length apart. First, at about 3:50 AM, four passengers from the French mail ship "Nusha" went ashore for sightseeing. After having dinner, they hired a sampan to return to the ship. One of the passengers, a Swiss man named Jie Weixie, fell asleep in the sampan. Suddenly, his body tilted, and he fell into the Huangpu River. The boatman urgently called for water police boats to search for him, but his body has not yet been found. He boarded the ship in Marseille, intending to go to Kobe for business. Unexpectedly, joy turned to sorrow, and he was buried in the Huangpu River. Unexpectedly, ten minutes later, at about 4:00 AM, an even more tragic accident occurred. Several French navy personnel were returning to the "Russo" warship in a sampan. When they reached a place not far from where the Swiss man fell into the river, one of them, for some unknown reason, suddenly quarreled with the boatman. He became angry and kicked the boatman directly into the Huangpu River. Afterwards, the water police station searched for him, but they were also unable to find his body. It is now reported that the head of the water police station, Wu Feide, and patrol chief Pu Na, are investigating, and officials from the municipal government have also started an investigation.

Family of Missing Elderly Man Scammed 139

▲ Bandits Send Letter Claiming Kidnapping

▲ Two Hundred Dollars Scammed Beside Coffin

Tang Shaoru, an elderly man of seventy-seven years old from Zhangyan, Jinshan, came to Shanghai for business. He suddenly contracted a hidden illness, so he sought medical treatment. His nerves were also disturbed. On the afternoon of the 16th of last month, at about 7:30 PM, he suddenly went missing. The fact that a reward had been offered for his search had been recorded in previous reports. It is now learned that the elderly man has been missing for a full month, and there is still no trace of him. However, his family in the countryside has been defrauded of silver dollars in a kidnapping scheme. The process was quite tortuous and interesting. The details are recorded below:

▲ Family Situation: Although Elder Tang is old, his body is very strong. He lives in Zhangyan North Street and runs the Tangtai Ji cured meat shop. He has no assets and can barely make ends meet. He has a wife and a son. His wife is also over fifty years old, and his son is only fourteen years old. He had a son late in life and loves him very much. He takes him everywhere. He personally selects and purchases goods for the shop, so he often needs to come to Shanghai. Whenever he arrives in Shanghai, he always stays at a friend's place in the French Concession. He walks briskly on the road and never hires a car to ride in.

▲ Sudden Unexpected Stimulus: In early August, Elder Tang came to Shanghai from his hometown to discuss business matters and stayed at his friend's residence. One evening, while walking along Avenue Edward VII, on the border of the British and French Concessions, he was forcibly pulled away by a prostitute. Unexpectedly, he contracted syphilis. Because of being forced to suffer this hidden illness, his brain was suddenly stimulated, and he was admitted to the hospital for treatment on August 11th, introduced by a friend. As a result, he was depressed and his nerves became disordered. Although the hidden illness gradually healed, his speech was still occasionally incoherent. It was originally planned that he would return to his hometown after a few more days of recovery.

▲ Circumstances of Disappearance: On the afternoon of September 16th, at about 7:30 PM, Elder Tang, who was fond of opium paste, went out of the hospital alone, intending to go somewhere to smoke it. Unexpectedly, he suddenly went missing on the way. When the hospital saw that he did not return, they thought he must have returned home. Later, his family came to Shanghai to visit and learned that he was indeed missing. At the time when Elder Tang left, he was only wearing a double blue twill short coat, willow cloth trousers, white gauze socks, and black shoes. He was bald, his hair was already snow-white, and he only had twenty-two silver dollars, a silver watch, and several hundred copper coins with him, and nothing else. Reports had been filed with various Chinese and foreign authorities, requesting an investigation.

▲ Letter Received Stating He Had Been Kidnapped: Later, the family sent out investigators in all directions, but there was no trace of him. While the family was anxiously surprised, they suddenly received a letter from Shanghai to their hometown at the end of September. It stated that Elder Tang was safe and sound in Shanghai, and that they only needed to prepare 1,500 silver dollars. After the full amount was paid, the person would be returned without fail. The reply could be sent by someone to Shanghai and placed in a broken shoe left on the ground east of the Xujiahui Railway Station. Therefore, the family knew that he had been kidnapped and a ransom was demanded. However, because they were concerned that his old age might lead to danger, they decided to tentatively negotiate.

▲ Process of Negotiation Between the Two Parties: Because people's hearts are treacherous, they were afraid that it was a scam to defraud them of money. So, they wrote a reply, requesting that the other party send back an item of Elder Tang's clothing as proof. As for the amount, they did not have the ability to pay that much and must reduce it. They sent someone to place the reply in the shoe at the specified address. After several days, another letter came, saying that it was difficult to send the item, and used Elder Tang's nickname, "Tang Bench," as proof. His family believed that this nickname was known to few outsiders, so they believed it was true. They communicated and negotiated the amount, and at the beginning of this month, the other party sent a letter, stating that they had agreed to prepare 400 dollars. First, pay 200 dollars and send someone

Page 16

to Shanghai and place it in a broken shoe next to the coffin in a thatched pavilion north of the Xujiahui Railway Road. As for the remaining 200 dollars, they would send another letter in a few days to arrange a place in the concession, next to the Central Hotel, for the exchange of people and money.

▲ Indeed, Money Lost and Scammed: The family naturally felt anxious and hoped for his return, considering his old age and illness. So, they prepared 200 dollars and sent someone to Shanghai to place it in the shoe at the specified address. The next day, the family eagerly waited for a letter arranging a date, so that they could hand over the money and pick up the person. Unexpectedly, ten days have passed, and there is no news. They realized that they had indeed been scammed. But he has been missing for a full month, and his fate is still unknown. The anxiety of his family cannot be described in words.

Young Man and Woman Fall in Love and Rashly Cohabit 140

▲ Both Man and Woman Are Under Twenty Years Old

▲ They Cohabited Soon After Falling in Love

▲ Parents Neglected to Prevent It in Advance

▲ Afterwards, They Reported to the Police Station for Arrest

▲ A Man and a Woman in the Neighborhood: The woman, Qu Xinnan, is only seventeen years old, beautiful, and lives with her mother, Qu Weng, at No. 76, Gujia Lane, Beijing Road, Zhejiang Road. Her son-in-law, Hai Rong, also lives there. There is a man named Gao Yuliang in the neighborhood, nineteen years old, handsome, who has long coveted Xinnan's beauty. In February of this year, Xinnan went out and met Gao, and they became attracted to each other.

▲ Like a Couple: Since then, they have been very close. After three months, Xinnan and Gao's passion had reached a boiling point. So, she entrusted her life to him, and Gao agreed. Xinnan's mother learned of this matter and, seeing that the die was cast, did not object. Gao then acted as if he owned the place and lived unconditionally with the Qu family, living with Xinnan as if they were a couple.

▲ The Good Date Was Delayed: At that time, Gao's father also knew about it and strongly disapproved of his son, severely reprimanding him. Gao, because of his strict father's obstruction, although he intended to marry her, dared not speak. Qu Weng and Xinnan, etc., were quite unhappy because the good date was delayed.

▲ Xinnan Was Expelled by Her Mother: On the evening of the 4th of this month, Gao went out on business. Qu Weng said harsh words about Gao to Xinnan and ordered Xinnan to leave and not return home. Xinnan was very angry when she heard this, so she secretly went out and lived at Room 16, Shanghai New Hotel, No. 249 Guangdong Road. Because her pockets were empty, she borrowed seven dollars from her younger sister, Che Ruiyun, to pay for the room.

▲ Newspaper Statement of Running Away: After Xinnan left, Qu Weng published a statement in the newspaper, saying that her daughter had run away with more than one hundred dollars and gold rings and gold buttons, etc. The daughter ignored this and discussed marriage matters with Gao. Unexpectedly, the matter was discovered by the daughter's maternal uncle, Weng Lyuxi, who found out where the girl was living. The night before last, he reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station. The police chief ordered detective Zhao Ziren and Western detective Ge Shi Li to go to the hotel at midnight and arrest the girl and Gao together and take them to the police station, where they were separately detained.

▲ Police Station Sues Gao Yuliang: Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Special District Court Criminal Division 1, where Judge Xu Jia Shi and Prosecutor Xu Mei took the bench to interrogate them. The police station lawyer, Ru Bao Yi, stated that the police station is now suing Gao Yuliang for the crime of enticing and abducting a man and a woman under the age of twenty, in violation of Article 257 of the Criminal Law, to leave the custody of a person enjoying parental rights, guardian, or protector. Qu Xinnan was not prosecuted, so Xinnan only remained in the status of witness. However, this accusation was made by the police station at the request of the accuser. He gave a detailed account of the facts of the case.

▲ Entrusting Her Life: Qu Weng stated that when Xinnan ran away, she also took away gold jewelry and money, etc. Qu Xinnan testified that she met Gao Yuliang in February of this year. After testing him for three months, I felt that he was quite reliable, so in May I entrusted my life to him, and a physical relationship occurred. This time, I was expelled by my mother, not seduced by Gao. When I went out, I did not take away anything. The hotel room rent was borrowed from someone else. My friend tried to find out my mother's tone, and my mother said that she definitely did not want me to go home, and my sister also said that if I go home again, what face would I have? So, I dare not return home. After I was arrested and taken to the police station, I asked to go out to tell his father and discuss marriage methods, because his father must come forward to handle this matter. But my mother and others firmly refused, leaving me detained in the police station overnight.

▲ Gao Yuliang's Statement: Che Ruiyun also testified that Qu Weng did not want her to return home after her daughter went out, breaking off the relationship between mother and daughter. The defendant, Gao Yuliang, testified that he lived at the plaintiff's house for more than a month. This time, I did not abduct Xinnan, but Xinnan ran out and invited me to the hotel.

▲ No Act of Enticement: Lawyer Ru Bao Yi asked Qu Weng whether she still needed to accuse Gao. Ms. Gao replied that she had to accuse him because Gao had seduced her daughter. Lawyer Ru then stated to the court that since the plaintiff still needed to continue the accusation, the police station seemed unable to withdraw the accusation. However, Qu Weng also admitted the relationship between the defendant and Qu Xinnan and the defendant's statement that he lived and ate at the plaintiff's house. Therefore, according to my lawyer's observation, the defendant did not commit any act of enticement and should be judged by the court. Judge Xu Jia Shi verified the testimony and declared Gao Yuliang not guilty in court.

▲ End of the Case: Qu Xinnan was taken back by her mother, Qu Weng. Later, it was heard that when Xinnan and Che Ruiyun returned to the Qu residence, Qu Weng and her younger brother beat Qu Xinnan. Che Ruiyun reported to Chinese detective Qiu En Jiu and has now reported to the Lao Zha Police Station. It is not yet known how it will be resolved.

Visiting the Water and Electricity Plants Requires Listening to the Instructions of Company Employees 142

▲ Wan Bamboo Student Drowns in Pool

▲ Municipal Public Works Bureau Plans to Prevent Danger

The day before yesterday (the 16th), students from the Municipal Wan Bamboo Primary School visited the inland water plant. A female student, Li Xiubao, accidentally fell into the pool. The pool was more than ten feet deep. By the time she was rescued and brought ashore, she was already unconscious and soon died. The Municipal Public Works Bureau, upon hearing the news, believed it was commendable that students could pay attention to public utilities and visit them together. However, they were saddened by this death. To plan for preventing danger, they specially sent a letter to the Education Bureau, instructing all schools in the city that if students visit the water and electricity plants in the future, in addition to the teachers in charge being fully responsible for protection, they must absolutely listen to the instructions of the company employees and stop moving forward when encountering areas where passage is prohibited. At the same time, they instructed the water and electricity companies that if people from all walks of life visit, they must assign personnel to guide them, and they must first explain the dangerous areas and prevent them from moving forward to prevent accidents.

A Lightweight Wireless Machine That Can Be Carried by Two People Appears 144

▲ Produced by China Tri-Pole Sharp Electric Company

▲ Total Weight of the Entire Machine Is More Than Forty Pounds

The China Tri-Pole Sharp Electric Company at the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Route Ferguson in this city has newly manufactured a compact shortwave wireless telegraph. The entire machine is divided into five parts: a transmitter box, a receiver box, a power box, a parts box, and an antenna pole. The parts, such as the antenna pole and transceiver box, are all made of steel bell. The power supply uses dry batteries. The total weight of the entire machine is more than forty kilograms, so it can be easily transported by two people. It is extremely light and convenient. (The picture on the right is a photo of the machine being transported.) It is said that the wireless telegraphs used in various places in China in the past used storage batteries, kerosene engines, and generators for power, so the entire machine was very bulky and could not be transported without a dozen or more people, and the operating procedures were also very troublesome. Now, the creation of this lightweight machine will greatly benefit society. It is said that the company has spent more than half a year of research on this machine and has made more than ten improvements before achieving today's success. The communication distance can reach about one thousand Chinese miles. The China United Wireless Electric Company at No. 3 Museum Road also sells it.

Garbage Incineration Plant to Begin Construction 145

▲ Expected to Be Completed in September Next Year

The disposal of garbage is a major problem in the Public Concession. The Board of Directors of the Public Works Department recently decided to add a Pelmer incinerator in the Eastern District, with a total cost of 365,000 taels for purchasing machinery and construction. Construction will begin this year and is expected to be completed in September next year. According to the director of the Public Works Department, Shanghai's garbage contains too much fresh vegetation and non-combustible materials, and too much water, which is different from the nature of garbage in London and New York. Therefore, the incineration methods used in the two cities cannot be applied. Now, the Pelmer method is popular in South America. According to his opinion, it is particularly suitable for destroying Shanghai's garbage. It also has a cremation room, which can dispose of dead animals. Its capacity is at least 170 tons of garbage per day. According to the Public Works Department, a German and Indfu Nuo incinerator has recently been ordered from abroad, which is planned to be installed on Binlang Road. In the future, there will be one in each of the east and west districts, and there will be no worry about where to dispose of the garbage in the concession.

A Bizarre Theft Case in Daxiang Lane 152

At approximately 8:00 AM yesterday, a box of leather clothing and miscellaneous silver dollars, worth approximately two hundred yuan, were stolen from the home of the Meng family, the sub-landlord at No. 11 Tianxiang Lane on Rue du Père Huc in the French Concession. The beginning and end of the theft case appear to be quite strange. The details are recorded as follows: The entire two-story building is rented by the Wu family, and the pavilion room is rented by the Gu family, both of whom work in the education sector. The front building on the third floor is occupied by the Wang family, who runs a carpentry business, and the rear building is occupied by the Xu family, who runs a sock factory. The pavilion room on the third floor is occupied by the Shen family, who are residents. However, both the Wang and Shen families moved in yesterday morning. The furniture is all made of mahogany. The lower floor is rented and occupied by the sub-landlord. On this day, because the tenants who moved in were all acquaintances, he specially prepared dishes to invite them to dine together. In the evening, they gathered again until eight o'clock, when he suddenly went out with someone to redeem a box of leather clothing that had been pawned the previous year from a pawnshop near Taiping Bridge. Upon returning, he felt extremely tired from the day's busyness. At about ten o'clock, he went to bed alone. After one watch, it was already past three o'clock. Suddenly, he faintly heard a sound coming from inside the room. Listening more carefully, it sounded like the sound of drawers and keys. Just as he was about to get up to check, he heard the sound of a kitten following one after another. Distinguishing carefully, it seemed not like a real cat, and he couldn't help but be surprised and puzzled. He immediately sat up and tried to turn on the electric light on the bed, but the mechanism had failed. His hair stood on end even more. He rushed out of the curtain and saw a bald, white-clothed, short figure rushing out. He immediately gave chase, but the thief had already rushed out of the door. He thought to himself that he was a lone woman, and the lights in the lane were already off. The night was as dark as ink. There was no police whistle, and he felt even more afraid to give chase. He had no choice but to retreat to the living room. When he turned on the light, he saw clothing scattered all over the floor. The drawers of the large cabinet were also moved out and placed upside down in the courtyard. Miscellaneous items were scattered. The boxes and chests in the room had all been moved. The leather clothing that had been redeemed that evening had all disappeared. He then cried out loudly, "Catch the thief! Catch the thief!" The neighbors were all awakened. At first, they thought it was a fire, and they all gathered to ask what had happened. At this time, the watchman and the water worker also arrived. They immediately investigated and found that the thief had entered and exited the lane through the large iron gate, which had been damaged beforehand. Then, he pried open the front door of the house to enter. According to the lane, the south side is directly connected to the general lane of Hengqing Lane. The watchman locks the front and rear iron gates every night at six o'clock and twelve o'clock and then patrols the old Tianxiang Lane on Beller Road. Therefore, the front door inside the lane is not often visited at night. Upon careful examination, the thief seemed to be quite familiar with the situation in the lane and knew the events of that evening in advance. Every step was prepared. Afterwards, the patrolman found a lost bill of lading, clothing, and copper items outside the iron gate on the west side of the road and returned them to their original owners. Afterwards, the victim issued a loss report to the Lujiawan Police Station in the jurisdiction for investigation. The head detective immediately ordered an investigation. It was also found that the front doors of No. 6 and No. 12, which are opposite the back door of the house and next door to the west, were also pried open at the same time, but they did not enter. Only this house was stolen, which makes it even more strange, it is said.

Fire on Datong Road, Zhabei 155

On Datong Road in Zhabei, near the intersection of Yongxing Road west of the Sun Temple, there is a vacant lot of approximately four mu, entirely covered with makeshift thatched huts, inhabited by laborers, approximately eighty or more rooms. Yesterday at 1:10 PM, one of the households, for unknown reasons, suddenly became careless. Because straw is easily combustible, and the west wind was very strong at the time, the fire spread rapidly and fiercely, consuming everything in its path. More than twenty thatched huts were completely destroyed. Fortunately, firefighters from various sections arrived and bravely poured water, preventing the fire from spreading completely. It was extinguished at 2:30 PM. After the fire started, the Fourth District Headquarters ordered the police to cooperate with the police officers from the Sun Temple Police Station to maintain order and arrested three suspects: Shi Xiubao, 42 years old, from Yancheng; Zhang Zhu, 25 years old, from Dongtai; and Teng Fan, 53 years old, from Yancheng. However, during the interrogation, each denied responsibility. Approximately fifty households were affected by the disaster, none of whom were insured. As autumn is ending and the weather is getting colder, it is pitiful that they have lost their homes. It was also reported that when the fire was raging, Gu Zhu tried to enter the house to move belongings and suffered burns to his left arm and slight injuries to his face, but he was not seriously injured.

Poor Couple Hang Themselves Due to Poverty 156

Han Kezi, a man from Jiangbei who lived in a thatched house at No. 24 near the Gongyi Yarn Factory on Route Robison in the western part of Shanghai, worked as a rickshaw puller. His wife, Zhang, had been ill for a long time, and they had no money for medical treatment. Overwhelmed by poverty and illness, she became resentful and filled with bitterness, leading her to contemplate suicide. Last night, while her husband was out pulling a rickshaw, she hanged herself with a belt. Although Han returned home and discovered it, he had no money for a coffin. The body lay exposed for two days and nights. Yesterday, the Sixth District Public Security Bureau learned of the situation and notified the local bailiff, who reported it to the local court. In the afternoon, a prosecutor and others were dispatched to the scene to confirm the death. Because the family was unable to afford a coffin, the court ordered the charity to provide a coffin and collect the body.

Robbers Arrested on Qiujiang Road 157

On the 17th of last month, the Cai Hongji Milk Shop in Zhabei was robbed. Stamp Duty on Chamber of Commerce Membership Certificates 160

▲Not Specified in the Stamp Tax Regulations

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Office of the Jiangsu Provincial Stamp Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, stating: "Regarding your letter stating that membership certificates of trade associations should be subject to stamp duty in accordance with the example of members of the Chamber of Commerce, which has been approved by the Ministry, please note and forward to all trade associations for compliance, etc. The main point of this case is that the Stamp Tax Regulations are decided by the Central Political Conference and have the nature of law. Since there is no provision in the regulations for the affixing of stamp duty to membership certificates of the Chamber of Commerce, according to the principle that orders cannot contradict the law, taxes not specified in the regulations cannot be forcibly imposed on the people. Furthermore, according to the original text of the Ministry of Finance's Document No. 13865 to the Ministry of Justice, the Ministry has not raised the issue of lawyer membership certificates being subject to stamp duty in accordance with the membership certificates of the Chamber of Commerce, but only stipulated that contracts and receipts should be subject to stamp duty and requested notification for compliance. This shows that the Ministry of Finance originally had no regulations regarding membership certificates of the Chamber of Commerce and has tacitly acknowledged that orders cannot change the law, so it no longer insists on its previous proposal. People are governed by the law and should be treated equally regardless of their class. How can lawyers be exempted from extra-legal taxes, while merchants can be subject to stamp duty by a ministerial order at any time outside the regulations? Therefore, our Chamber believes that the affixing of stamp duty to membership certificates of the Chamber of Commerce should also be done as claimed by the Zhejiang Stamp Tax Bureau, only after supplementing and revising the Stamp Tax Regulations. This is not only true for membership certificates of various trade associations. Accordingly, we have prepared a letter to provide a detailed reply for your review."

Problems Arise at the National Goods Emporium 161

▲Allowed to Reopen Only After Fulfilling License Conditions

The Shanghai Times reported that at the board meeting of the Public Works Department the other day, Chief Executive Edward stated that the arrangement and equipment of the National Goods Emporium in the old Municipal Hall failed to comply with the conditions listed in the Public Works Department license, which would be extremely dangerous in the event of a fire. After deliberation by the directors, it was considered that if the emporium unfortunately caught fire, the Public Works Department would bear significant responsibility. Therefore, although some directors advocated extending the deadline for a few more days, ordering the emporium manager to complete the arrangement in accordance with the license regulations within the deadline, the discussion ultimately decided to instruct the police to go and order the emporium to close until the indoor equipment could fulfill the conditions listed in the license before being allowed to reopen.

Jishan Society's Recent Relief Efforts for Shaanxi Disaster 162

The Chinese Jishan Society in this city recently received a letter from the Chang'an Jishan Branch in Shaanxi, stating that they had received the total of nine thousand six hundred yuan in disaster relief funds and expenses for the disaster relief orphanage, which had been duly received and telegraphed back. The three Wugong disaster relief orphanages were receiving children whose situation had worsened and had no place to seek refuge. The seven and eight months extension had now expired, and the children's survival was endangered. In addition, locust plagues in Shaanxi were devastating crops, filling the sky and covering the land. Although the government had repeatedly issued locust control notices, promoted agricultural achievements, and made every effort to defend against the locusts, the locust damage was too severe, the autumn harvest was hopeless, and the number of disaster victims was increasing daily. As autumn was approaching and the weather was getting colder, winter relief efforts should be initiated in advance, including providing cotton clothing or disaster relief funds. It was hoped that careful planning would be done and attention paid to it early. The branch had distributed approximately 20,000 yuan worth of wheat seeds in the north and south mountains and Chang'an counties, which had exhausted its resources. The disaster victims were pleading and appealing from all sides, which it could not cope with. In the middle of the night, it was difficult to sleep. The pagoda was being built, and the voyage was landing. All these hopes were placed on the general assembly, it was said. It was found that the society had spent a considerable amount of money on disaster relief in Shaanxi in the past two years. Now that the disaster has worsened and the livelihood of the disaster victims has become more difficult, the society is unable to support it alone. Recently, it telegraphed the Shaanxi Society, agreeing to allocate an additional two months of expenses for the Wugong disaster relief orphanage, totaling 3,000 yuan, to be remitted to Shaanxi for emergency relief. Other severely affected areas will still be planned for at any time, in the hope of saving as many lives as possible.

Aunt Does Not Approve of Nephew Cooking 163

▲Flying Brick Injures Head

Zhu Deben, 36 years old, from Yancheng, earns a living by pulling a rickshaw. Because he has no family in Shanghai, he resides at the home of his maternal uncle, Zhou, at No. 26 Taisen Lane on Ping'an Bridge in the South City, paying a monthly rent of two yuan. However, meals are not included, and he eats at small restaurants every day. Recently, as the weather has gotten colder, Zhu found it inconvenient to buy food outside, so he bought a pot and stove to cook for himself in his room. When his aunt, Yan, saw this, she felt that it obstructed her coming and going and immediately interfered. Zhu then appealed to his uncle, Zhou, asking for his support. Zhou scolded his wife, saying that his nephew was cooking in his room and that she had no right to interfere. They disagreed and a conflict arose. Yan fell to the ground and was injured in the head, with blood flowing profusely. Her condition was very dangerous. She then ran out injured and reported the incident to Chen Jiaxiang, the watchman at the 20th post. Chen took Zhu to the First Section of the First District Police Station. During the preliminary hearing by the station chief, Yan stated that her nephew, Zhu Deben, wanted to set up a stove in her house to cook, but she refused. He then told his uncle, who is her husband. Unexpectedly, he became angry and beat her. Because she was not fully recovered from her illness, she was unable to defend herself. She accused her nephew of helping to commit the crime, saying that her nephew picked up a brick from the ground and threw it at her, hitting her head, causing her to be injured and bleed. She requested a thorough investigation. The station chief, considering the matter a case of assault, ordered a document to be prepared and transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for interrogation.

▲Sentenced to Thirty Days of Detention

▲Gun License Revoked

Judge Xu reviewed the statements and sentenced Zhang Jingui to thirty days of detention for endangering life and threatening others, causing harm to their safety. The number of days of detention prior to the final judgment was allowed to offset the detention for one day. The pistol was returned to Sun Jingru for collection, and Zhang Jingui's gun license was revoked.

Letters to the Editor 174

October 14th. The news report in your newspaper regarding Zhao Dingyu, a partner at the Fukang Paper Shop at No. 149 Huajin Road in the city, transporting copper coins, is inconsistent with the facts. We respectfully present the facts as they occurred at the time and hope that you will publish them in the "Letters to the Editor" section for correction. We would be grateful. Upon investigation, on the 14th of this month, our shop sent partner Zhao Dingyu to the Nanshi district to purchase and dismantle copper coins. At the Heshun Paper Shop at No. 686 Waima Road, he inquired and found that there were copper coins available for exchange. He purchased 100 yuan worth of copper coins, totaling 283,000. On the way back in a carriage, while passing through Wanyu Wharf Street, he was stopped by the police from the First District, First Precinct, who suspected him of being a private seller from Jiangbei coming to Shanghai. He was immediately taken to the precinct. Subsequently, the chief of the precinct investigated and determined that he had purchased the copper coins for exchange at the Heshun Paper Shop and that he had made a profit of only a little over ten cash at the current price. The copper coins were then returned to him with a receipt. This matter concerns the reputation of our shop. We respectfully request a correction. Fukang Paper Shop respectfully submitted.

Respectfully submitted. We have recently read in your newspaper about Fang Shouchun leaving a note and fleeing. It was mistakenly reported that Fang was a partner in our shop. In reality, Fang was a friend of a partner in our shop. He was originally a dealer in southern goods in his hometown of Yuyao. Due to family problems, he came to Shanghai in a fit of pique and stayed at the New Gaosheng Hotel, not on the upper floor of our shop. His uncle, Fang Lanting, works as a teacher at Lao Jiulun, and his cousin, Jie Fu (not an older cousin), works as a buyer of foreign goods in Gujia Lane. The person who reported it to the water police was his cousin Jie Fu and a partner from our shop. It has nothing to do with our shop. We sincerely fear misunderstandings from the outside world and hereby request your newspaper to quickly make a correction. We would be grateful. Respectfully submitted to the editor of Shen Bao. Gongping Sock Factory, October 18th.
